```json
{
  "content": "//! JSON-RPC 2.0 stdio server for MCP.\n\nuse std::io::{self, BufRead, Write};\n\nuse anyhow::Result;\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse serde_json::{json, Value};\n\nuse crate::adapters::{dedup_sessions, ClaudeCode, ConvoAdapter, WorkspaceScope};\nuse crate::render::{render_markdown, MarkdownOptions};\nuse crate::transform::{apply_path_rewrite, PathRewrite};\n\npub const PROTOCOL_VERSION: &str = \"2024-11-05\";\npub const SERVER_NAME: &str = \"portaconv\";\npub const SERVER_VERSION: &str = env!(\"CARGO_PKG_VERSION\");\n\npub fn run_stdio_server() -> Result<()> {\n    let stdin = io::stdin();\n    let stdout = io::stdout();\n    let mut stdout = stdout.lock();\n\n    for line in stdin.lock().lines() {\n        let line = match line {\n            Ok(l) => l,\n            Err(_) => break,\n        };\n        let line = line.trim();\n        if line.is_empty() {\n            continue;\n        }\n\n        let req: Value = match serde_json::from_str(line) {\n            Ok(v) => v,\n            Err(e) => {\n                write_response(\n                    &mut stdout,\n                    &error_response(Value::Null, -32700, &format!(\"parse error: {e}\")),\n                )?;\n                continue;\n            }\n        };\n\n        let id = req.get(\"id\").cloned().unwrap_or(Value::Null);\n        let method = req.get(\"method\").and_then(|m| m.as_str()).unwrap_or(\"\");\n        let params = req.get(\"params\").cloned().unwrap_or(Value::Null);\n\n        // Notifications (no `id`) never get a response body — but the\n        // server still dispatches side-effects if relevant. v0.1 has\n        // no side-effect notifications to honor, so we just drop them.\n        let is_notification = req.get(\"id\").is_none();\n\n        let response = dispatch(method, params);\n        if is_notification {\n            continue;\n        }\n\n        let envelope = match response {\n            Ok(result) => success_response(id, result),\n            Err((code, msg)) => error_response(id, code, &msg),\n        };\n        write_response(&mut stdout, &envelope)?;\n    }\n\n    Ok(())\n}\n\nfn write_response(out: &mut impl Write, v: &Value) -> io::Result<()> {\n    let s = serde_json::to_string(v).unwrap_or_else(|_| \"{}\".into());\n    writeln!(out, \"{s}\")?;\n    out.flush()\n}\n\nfn success_response(id: Value, result: Value) -> Value {\n    json!({\n        \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\",\n        \"id\": id,\n        \"result\": result,\n    })\n}\n\nfn error_response(id: Value, code: i32, message: &str) -> Value {\n    json!({\n        \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\",\n        \"id\": id,\n        \"error\": { \"code\": code, \"message\": message },\n    })\n}\n\nfn dispatch(method: &str, params: Value) -> Result<Value, (i32, String)> {\n    match method {\n        \"initialize\" => Ok(initialize_result()),\n        \"ping\" => Ok(json!({})),\n        \"tools/list\" => Ok(tools_list()),\n        \"tools/call\" => tools_call(params),\n        \"resources/list\" => Ok(resources_list()),\n        \"resources/read\" => resources_read(params),\n        // Notifications MCP clients send but don't require response:\n        \"notifications/initialized\"\n        | \"notifications/cancelled\"\n        | \"notifications/roots/list_changed\" => Ok(Value::Null),\n        other => Err((-32601, format!(\"method not found: {other}\"))),\n    }\n}\n\nfn initialize_result() -> Value {\n    json!({\n        \"protocolVersion\": PROTOCOL_VERSION,\n        \"serverInfo\": {\n            \"name\": SERVER_NAME,\n            \"version\": SERVER_VERSION,\n        },\n        \"capabilities\": {\n            \"tools\": {},\n            \"resources\": { \"listChanged\": false, \"subscribe\": false },\n        },\n    })\n}\n\nfn tools_list() -> Value {\n    json!({\n        \"tools\": [\n            {\n                \"name\": \"list_conversations\",\n                \"description\": \"List Claude Code conversations discoverable on this machine. Returns SessionMeta entries with id, cwd, started_at, updated_at, message_count, source_path.\",\n                \"inputSchema\": {\n                    \"type\": \"object\",\n                    \"properties\": {\n                        \"min_messages\": {\n                            \"type\": \"integer\",\n                            \"description\": \"Hide sessions with fewer than this many messages (default 1).\"\n                        },\n                        \"show_duplicates\": {\n                            \"type\": \"boolean\",\n                            \"description\": \"Return every physical-file entry; default false collapses WSL/Windows-encoded duplicates.\"\n                        },\n                        \"workspace_toml\": {\n                            \"type\": \"string\",\n                            \"description\": \"Scope by a portagenty workspace TOML. Accepts an explicit path or the literal string 'auto' to walk up from cwd.\"\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n            },\n            {\n                \"name\": \"get_conversation\",\n                \"description\": \"Load and render one session. Default format is paste-ready markdown. Path-rewrite transforms are opt-in.\",\n                \"inputSchema\": {\n                    \"type\": \"object\",\n                    \"required\": [\"id\"],\n                    \"properties\": {\n                        \"id\": { \"type\": \"string\", \"description\": \"Session UUID.\" },\n                        \"format\": {\n                            \"type\": \"string\",\n                            \"enum\": [\"markdown\", \"json\"],\n                            \"description\": \"Output format (default: markdown).\"\n                        },\n                        \"rewrite\": {\n                            \"type\": \"string\",\n                            \"enum\": [\"wsl-to-win\", \"win-to-wsl\", \"strip\"],\n                            \"description\": \"Opt-in OS-path rewriting on content (NOT cwd metadata).\"\n                        },\n                        \"include_thinking\": {\n                            \"type\": \"boolean\",\n                            \"description\": \"Include assistant thinking blocks in markdown output (default false).\"\n                        },\n                        \"full_results\": {\n                            \"type\": \"boolean\",\n                            \"description\": \"Emit full tool-result bodies (default false — truncated at 600 chars).\"\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        ]\n    })\n}\n\nfn tools_call(params: Value) -> Result<Value, (i32, String)> {\n    #[derive(Deserialize)]\n    struct Envelope {\n        name: String,\n        #[serde(default)]\n        arguments: Value,\n    }\n    let env: Envelope = serde_json::from_value(params)\n        .map_err(|e| (-32602, format!(\"invalid tools/call params: {e}\")))?;\n\n    match env.name.as_str() {\n        \"list_conversations\" => list_conversations(env.arguments),\n        \"get_conversation\" => get_conversation(env.arguments),\n        other => Err((-32601, format!(\"tool not found: {other}\"))),\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Deserialize, Default)]\nstruct ListArgs {\n    min_messages: Option<usize>,\n    show_duplicates: Option<bool>,\n    workspace_toml: Option<String>,\n}\n\nfn list_conversations(args: Value) -> Result<Value, (i32, String)> {\n    let args: ListArgs = serde_json::from_value(args)\n        .map_err(|e| (-32602, format!(\"invalid list_conversations args: {e}\")))?;\n    let adapter = ClaudeCode;\n    if !adapter.detect() {\n        return Err((-32603, \"Claude Code storage not detected\".into()));\n    }\n    let scope = build_scope(args.workspace_toml.as_deref())\n        .map_err(|e| (-32603, format!(\"workspace scope: {e:#}\")))?;\n    let mut metas = adapter\n        .list(Some(&scope))\n        .map_err(|e| (-32603, format!(\"list failed: {e:#}\")))?;\n    let min = args.min_messages.unwrap_or(1);\n    metas.retain(|m| m.message_count >= min);\n    if !args.show_duplicates.unwrap_or(false) {\n        metas = dedup_sessions(metas);\n    }\n    // MCP tools return a `content` array of content items; a JSON\n    // payload lands as a text block containing its JSON string. Clients\n    // parse this themselves — the schema here matches the convention\n    // used by other MCP servers.\n    let payload = serde_json::to_string(&metas)\n        .map_err(|e| (-32603, format!(\"serialize: {e}\")))?;\n    Ok(json!({\n        \"content\": [ { \"type\": \"text\", \"text\": payload } ]\n    }))\n}\n\n#[derive(Deserialize)]\nstruct GetArgs {\n    id: String,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    format: Option<String>,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    rewrite: Option<String>,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    include_thinking: Option<bool>,\n    #[serde(default)]\n    full_results: Option<bool>,\n}\n\nfn get_conversation(args: Value) -> Result<Value, (i32, String)> {\n    let args: GetArgs = serde_json::from_value(args)\n        .map_err(|e| (-32602, format!(\"invalid get_conversation args: {e}\")))?;\n    let adapter = ClaudeCode;\n    if !adapter.detect() {\n        return Err((-32603, \"Claude Code storage not detected\".into()));\n    }\n    let mut conv = adapter\n        .load(&args.id)\n        .map_err(|e| (-32603, format!(\"load failed: {e:#}\")))?;\n    if let Some(kind) = args.rewrite.as_deref() {\n        let mode = parse_rewrite(kind)\n            .map_err(|e| (-32602, format!(\"invalid rewrite: {e}\")))?;\n        apply_path_rewrite(&mut conv, mode);\n    }\n    let body = match args.format.as_deref().unwrap_or(\"markdown\") {\n        \"markdown\" => {\n            let opts = MarkdownOptions {\n                include_thinking: args.include_thinking.unwrap_or(false),\n                full_results: args.full_results.unwrap_or(false),\n                ..MarkdownOptions::default()\n            };\n            render_markdown(&conv, &opts)\n        }\n        \"json\" => serde_json::to_string_pretty(&conv)\n            .map_err(|e| (-32603, format!(\"serialize: {e}\")))?,\n        other => return Err((-32602, format!(\"unknown format: {other}\"))),\n    };\n    Ok(json!({\n        \"content\": [ { \"type\": \"text\", \"text\": body } ]\n    }))\n}\n\nfn parse_rewrite(kind: &str) -> Result<PathRewrite, String> {\n    match kind {\n        \"wsl-to-win\" => Ok(PathRewrite::WslToWin),\n        \"win-to-wsl\" => Ok(PathRewrite::WinToWsl),\n        \"strip\" => Ok(PathRewrite::Strip),\n        other => Err(format!(\"unknown rewrite mode: {other}\")),\n    }\n}\n\n/// Advertise one resource-template — the concrete resource list is\n/// `resources/list` and would require enumerating every session, which\n/// is expensive. MCP's `resources/templates/list` is the idiomatic home\n/// for a URI template; until we wire that separately we surface the\n/// template here and return an empty flat list.\nfn resources_list() -> Value {\n    json!({\n        \"resources\": [],\n        \"resourceTemplates\": [\n            {\n                \"uriTemplate\": \"convos://conversation/{id}\",\n                \"name\": \"Conversation\",\n                \"description\": \"A Claude Code conversation rendered as paste-ready markdown.\",\n                \"mimeType\": \"text/markdown\"\n            }\n        ]\n    })\n}\n\n#[derive(Deserialize)]\nstruct ResourceReadArgs {\n    uri: String,\n}\n\nfn resources_read(params: Value) -> Result<Value, (i32, String)> {\n    let args: ResourceReadArgs = serde_json::from_value(params)\n        .map_err(|e| (-32602, format!(\"invalid resources/read params: {e}\")))?;\n    let id = args\n        .uri\n        .strip_prefix(\"convos://conversation/\")\n        .ok_or_else(|| {\n            (\n                -32602,\n                format!(\"unsupported resource URI: {} (expected convos://conversation/<id>)\", args.uri),\n            )\n        })?;\n    let adapter = ClaudeCode;\n    if !adapter.detect() {\n        return Err((-32603, \"Claude Code storage not detected\".into()));\n    }\n    let conv = adapter\n        .load(id)\n        .map_err(|e| (-32603, format!(\"load failed: {e:#}\")))?;\n    let md = render_markdown(&conv, &MarkdownOptions::default());\n    Ok(json!({\n        \"contents\": [\n            {\n                \"uri\": args.uri,\n                \"mimeType\": \"text/markdown\",\n                \"text\": md\n            }\n        ]\n    }))\n}\n\nfn build_scope(flag: Option<&str>) -> Result<WorkspaceScope> {\n    crate::cli::build_workspace_scope_public(flag)\n}\n\n/// Forwarding re-export for the MCP module. The CLI owns the workspace\n/// resolver; this avoids duplicating the walk-up logic.\n#[allow(dead_code)]\n#[derive(Serialize)]\nstruct _Marker;\n",
  "file_path": "/mnt/c/Users/Cybersader/Documents/1 Projects, Workspaces/portaconv/src/mcp/server.rs"
}
```

```json
{
  "content": "//! End-to-end MCP server tests via stdin/stdout. Same fixture corpus\n//! as `tests/cli.rs` so the adapter-level correctness is shared.\n\nuse std::path::PathBuf;\nuse std::process::{Command, Stdio};\nuse std::io::Write;\n\nuse serde_json::{json, Value};\n\nfn fixture_root() -> PathBuf {\n    let mut p = PathBuf::from(env!(\"CARGO_MANIFEST_DIR\"));\n    p.push(\"tests/fixtures/claude-projects\");\n    p\n}\n\nfn pconv_bin() -> PathBuf {\n    assert_cmd::cargo::cargo_bin(\"pconv\")\n}\n\n/// Send a batch of requests, capture stdout lines, parse each.\nfn roundtrip(requests: &[Value]) -> Vec<Value> {\n    let mut cmd = Command::new(pconv_bin())\n        .arg(\"mcp\")\n        .arg(\"serve\")\n        .env(\"PORTACONV_CLAUDE_ROOT\", fixture_root())\n        .stdin(Stdio::piped())\n        .stdout(Stdio::piped())\n        .stderr(Stdio::piped())\n        .spawn()\n        .expect(\"spawn pconv mcp serve\");\n\n    {\n        let stdin = cmd.stdin.as_mut().expect(\"stdin\");\n        for req in requests {\n            writeln!(stdin, \"{}\", serde_json::to_string(req).unwrap()).unwrap();\n        }\n        // Closing stdin (via drop at end of block) signals EOF; the\n        // server loop exits naturally.\n    }\n\n    let out = cmd.wait_with_output().expect(\"wait\");\n    String::from_utf8(out.stdout)\n        .expect(\"utf8\")\n        .lines()\n        .filter(|l| !l.trim().is_empty())\n        .map(|l| serde_json::from_str(l).expect(\"json-rpc line\"))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn initialize_handshake() {\n    let resps = roundtrip(&[json!({\n        \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\",\n        \"id\": 1,\n        \"method\": \"initialize\",\n        \"params\": { \"protocolVersion\": \"2024-11-05\", \"capabilities\": {} }\n    })]);\n    assert_eq!(resps.len(), 1);\n    let r = &resps[0];\n    assert_eq!(r[\"id\"], 1);\n    assert_eq!(r[\"result\"][\"serverInfo\"][\"name\"], \"portaconv\");\n    assert_eq!(r[\"result\"][\"protocolVersion\"], \"2024-11-05\");\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn tools_list_describes_both_tools() {\n    let resps = roundtrip(&[json!({\n        \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\", \"id\": 2, \"method\": \"tools/list\"\n    })]);\n    let tools = resps[0][\"result\"][\"tools\"].as_array().unwrap();\n    let names: Vec<&str> = tools.iter().map(|t| t[\"name\"].as_str().unwrap()).collect();\n    assert!(names.contains(&\"list_conversations\"));\n    assert!(names.contains(&\"get_conversation\"));\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn list_conversations_returns_fixture_session() {\n    let resps = roundtrip(&[json!({\n        \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\", \"id\": 3, \"method\": \"tools/call\",\n        \"params\": { \"name\": \"list_conversations\", \"arguments\": {} }\n    })]);\n    let text = resps[0][\"result\"][\"content\"][0][\"text\"].as_str().unwrap();\n \"aaaaaaaa-bbbb-cccc-dddd-000000000001\");\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn get_conversation_returns_markdown_by_default() {\n    let resps = roundtrip(&[json!({\n        \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\", \"id\": 4, \"method\": \"tools/call\",\n        \"params\": {\n            \"name\": \"get_conversation\",\n            \"arguments\": { \"id\": \"aaaaaaaa-bbbb-cccc-dddd-000000000001\" }\n        }\n    })]);\n    let text = resps[0][\"result\"][\"content\"][0][\"text\"].as_str().unwrap();\n    assert!(text.starts_with(\"# \"));\n    assert!(text.contains(\"## User\"));\n    assert!(text.contains(\"## Assistant\"));\n    assert!(text.contains(\"**tool call:**\"));\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn resources_read_matches_get_conversation_markdown() {\n    let resps = roundtrip(&[\n        json!({\n            \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\", \"id\": 1, \"method\": \"tools/call\",\n            \"params\": {\n                \"name\": \"get_conversation\",\n                \"arguments\": { \"id\": \"aaaaaaaa-bbbb-cccc-dddd-000000000001\" }\n            }\n        }),\n        json!({\n            \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\", \"id\": 2, \"method\": \"resources/read\",\n            \"params\": { \"uri\": \"convos://conversation/aaaaaaaa-bbbb-cccc-dddd-000000000001\" }\n        }),\n    ]);\n    let via_tool = resps[0][\"result\"][\"content\"][0][\"text\"].as_str().unwrap();\n    let via_resource = resps[1][\"result\"][\"contents\"][0][\"text\"].as_str().unwrap();\n    assert_eq!(via_tool, via_resource);\n    assert_eq!(\n        resps[1][\"result\"][\"contents\"][0][\"mimeType\"],\n        \"text/markdown\"\n    );\n}\n\n#[test]\nfn unknown_method_returns_32601() {\n    let resps = roundtrip(&[json!({\n        \"jsonrpc\": \"2.0\", \"id\": 1, \"method\": \"nope/whatever\"\n    })]);\n ```json
```
```json
{
  "content": "---\ntitle: Agents + portagenty\ndescription: How to wire portaconv into agent workflows — CLI calls, MCP server, and portagenty workspace scoping.\nsidebar:\n  order: 2\n---\n\nimport { Aside, Tabs, TabItem } from \"@astrojs/starlight/components\";\n\nportaconv exists so agents (and humans) can **shovel context around** —\nrecover from a `/compact`, hand a session off to a different tool,\npaste yesterday's reasoning into today's fresh agent, or commit\nmeaningful context slices into a repo. Two integration surfaces\ncover this: the CLI (any agent that runs shell commands) and the\nMCP server (agents speaking Model Context Protocol).\n\n## Two ways an agent reaches portaconv\n\n<div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr; gap: 0.75rem; margin: 1.5rem 0;\">\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-blue); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.9rem 1rem; background: var(--sl-color-blue-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">CLI — any agent with Bash tool</div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.85; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">\n      Agent runs <code>pconv list</code> / <code>pconv dump &lt;id&gt;</code> through its shell-execution tool. No extra wiring. Works in Claude Code, opencode, Aider, terminal-bound agents.\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.75rem; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.7;\">latency: fork+exec + walk · structured output: --format json</div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-accent); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.9rem 1rem; background: var(--sl-color-accent-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">MCP — agents speaking the protocol</div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.85; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">\n      Start <code>pconv mcp serve</code> from the agent's <code>mcp.json</code>. Two typed tools + a URI-templated resource. Agent calls them like any other MCP server.\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.75rem; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.7;\">latency: in-process JSON-RPC · structured output: schema-validated</div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n## CLI — agent-callable via Bash tool\n\nA Claude Code session or any shell-capable agent can just run the\nbinary. The `--format json` flag on `list` and the default markdown\noutput on `dump` keep the agent's downstream parsing simple.\n\n```sh\n# Discover sessions belonging to the current workspace\npconv list --workspace-toml auto --format json\n\n# Dump a specific session for context recovery, with path rewriting\npconv dump <session-id> --rewrite wsl-to-win\n\n# Pipe to a recovery doc and commit it\npconv dump <session-id> > docs/agent-context/2026-04-20-recovery.md\ngit add docs/agent-context/ && git commit -m \"capture recovery context\"\n```\n\n<Aside type=\"tip\" title=\"Agent-ergonomics defaults\">\nExit codes are standard (`0` success, `1` any error, stderr carries\nthe message). `--format json` on `list` gives the agent a clean\nstructured list it can pipe into `jq` or re-parse. `dump`'s markdown\ndefault is tuned for re-pasting into an agent, not for human\nreading — short, hierarchical, tool-call-preserving.\n</Aside>\n\n## MCP — tools + resources over stdio\n\n`pconv mcp serve` speaks JSON-RPC 2.0 over stdio, line-delimited.\nDrop this into any MCP-capable agent's config:\n\n<Tabs>\n  <TabItem label=\"Claude Code\">\n    Claude Code reads `~/.claude/mcp.json` (or a project-local\n    `.mcp.json`) at launch. Add:\n\n    ```json\n    {\n      \"mcpServers\": {\n        \"portaconv\": {\n          \"command\": \"pconv\",\n          \"args\": [\"mcp\", \"serve\"]\n        }\n      }\n    }\n    ```\n  </TabItem>\n  <TabItem label=\"opencode\">\n    opencode uses a similar config shape. See its docs for the exact\n    path — the `command` + `args` pair is portable.\n  </TabItem>\n</Tabs>\n\n### Exposed tools\n\n<div style=\"background: var(--sl-color-gray-6); border-radius: 8px; padding: 1rem; margin: 1.5rem 0; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.82rem;\">\n<pre style=\"margin: 0;\"><code>{`list_conversations {\n  min_messages?:   integer      // default 1\n  show_duplicates?: boolean     // default false — collapse WSL/Win dups\n  workspace_toml?: string       // path, or \"auto\" to walk up from cwd\n}\n→ JSON-serialized SessionMeta[] (in content[0].text)\n\nget_conversation {\n  id:               string      // required — session UUID\n  format?:          \"markdown\" | \"json\"   // default markdown\n  rewrite?:         \"wsl-to-win\" | \"win-to-wsl\" | \"strip\"\n  include_thinking?: boolean    // default false\n  full_results?:    boolean     // default false — results truncated at 600 chars\n}\n→ rendered body (in content[0].text)`}</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n### Exposed resources\n\nOne URI template:\n\n```\nconvos://conversation/{id}\n```\n\n`resources/read` on a concrete URI returns the session as markdown\nwith the default renderer options. Equivalent to calling\n`get_conversation` with no optional args. Useful when an agent's\nUI exposes a \"resources\" picker distinct from tool calls.\n\n## Portagenty workspace scoping\n\nportagenty's workspace TOML (`*.portagenty.toml`) declares:\n\n- a stable `id` (UUID, survives folder moves)\n- a `projects` list — absolute or `~`-relative paths that belong to this workspace\n\nPoint portaconv at the TOML and `list` filters to just those\nprojects:\n\n```sh\n# Auto — walks up from cwd looking for *.portagenty.toml\npconv list --workspace-toml auto\n\n# Explicit path — works from anywhere\npconv list --workspace-toml /path/to/my-workspace.portagenty.toml\n```\n\nSame flag works via MCP as the `workspace_toml` argument on\n`list_conversations`. When `projects` is missing from the TOML,\nthe scope defaults to the TOML's own directory.\n\n<Aside type=\"note\" title=\"Why workspace scoping matters for agents\">\nAn agent running inside workspace A should see A's sessions, not every conversation on the machine. Without scoping, a <code>list_conversations</code> call returns the full corpus (~hundreds for a long-time user), blowing the context budget. Workspace-scoped listing keeps the agent focused.\n</Aside>\n\n## Patterns\n\n### 1. Post-`/compact` recovery\n\nAfter `/compact` in Claude Code, long-context detail is summarized.\nIf the agent later needs pre-compact specifics:\n\n```\n# From the agent:\npconv list --workspace-toml auto --format json\n# (agent picks the relevant old session UUID from the list)\npconv dump <old-session-id> --full-results > /tmp/pre-compact.md\n# (agent reads the file or inlines the content)\n```\n\n### 2. Cross-tool handoff\n\nSession authored in Claude Code on WSL, continuing in opencode on\nWindows:\n\n```\npconv dump <id> --rewrite wsl-to-win | clip.exe\n# paste into opencode, which reads the now-Windows-native paths\n```\n\n### 3. Committed recovery artifact\n\nFreeze an important session as a repo-tracked doc so it survives\nClaude Code's retention or a folder move:\n\n```\nmkdir -p docs/agent-context/\npconv dump <id> --full-results > docs/agent-context/$(date +%F)-redesign-session.md\ngit add docs/agent-context/ && git commit -m \"capture redesign context\"\n```\n\nRe-load it later by pointing a fresh agent at the committed file.\nNo daemon, no retention dependency — git is the store.\n\n### 4. Agent-as-curator via MCP\n\nAn agent already inside a session calls\n`list_conversations({ workspace_toml: \"auto\" })`, picks the\nmost-relevant prior session, calls `get_conversation({ id, format: \"markdown\", include_thinking: false })`,\nand prepends the result to its own working context. The user never\nhas to copy anything.\n\n## What portaconv doesn't do\n\n<div style=\"border-left: 4px solid var(--sl-color-orange); padding: 0.6rem 1rem; margin: 1.5rem 0; background: var(--sl-color-orange-low); font-size: 0.9rem;\">\n<ul style=\"margin: 0; padding-left: 1.2rem;\">\n  <li>Doesn't write back to any tool's storage. <em>Ever.</em></li>\n  <li>Doesn't run a daemon / watcher / background sync.</li>\n  <li>Doesn't manage clipboards — pipe to <code>clip.exe</code> / <code>pbcopy</code> / <code>wl-copy</code> yourself.</li>\n  <li>Doesn't do full-text search — get-by-id only in v0.1 (search tracked for v0.2+).</li>\n  <li>Doesn't know about portagenty's runtime state — only reads the TOML file at call time.</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n## Planned portagenty shim (not v0.1)\n\nThe eventual `pa convos` subcommand will shell out to `pconv` with\nworkspace context pre-filled:\n\n```\n# Shorthand for: pconv list --workspace-toml <this-workspace>\npa convos list\n\n# Shorthand for: pconv dump <id> piped with reasonable defaults\npa convos dump <id>\n\n# Surfaced when pa's auto-re-register-on-walk-up detects a folder\n# move — prompts the user to run pconv to see old-path sessions.\n```\n\nThis ships as a separate PR in the portagenty repo once portaconv\nreaches v0.1 publish. portaconv stays usable standalone.\n",
  "file_path": "/mnt/c/Users/Cybersader/Documents/1 Projects, Workspaces/portaconv/docs/src/content/docs/concepts/agents-and-portagenty.mdx"
}
```

## User

perf cache is a good start.  I'm not familiar with what crates.io does

## Assistant

## Assistant

**crates.io** is Rust's package registry — the equivalent of npm for JavaScript or PyPI for Python. When `pconv` is published there, anyone can install it with `cargo install portaconv` without cloning the repo. Right now people have to clone + `cargo install --path .`; crates.io eliminates that friction (plus gets you automatic API docs at docs.rs, download stats, and a permanent versioned home). Publishing is a one-time `cargo publish` after `cargo login`, then bumped versions get re-published as you ship.

Building the perf cache now.

## Assistant

**tool call:** `Write`

```json
{
  "content": "//! On-disk cache of `list()` scan results.\n//!\n//! A full walk of `~/.claude/projects/` with line-scans per JSONL takes\n//! ~50 s on a ~5 GB / 2607-file corpus. Most of that work is repeated:\n//! for unchanged files, every run re-parses the same bytes. This module\n//! memoizes per-file scan output, keyed by the tuple that guarantees\n//! validity: `(path, mtime_ns, size)`.\n//!\n//! Design rules the cache respects:\n//! - **Convenience, not source of truth.** A missing/corrupt/stale\n//!   cache falls back to a full scan. portaconv's extract-on-demand\n//!   philosophy still holds — the cache is just memoized work.\n//! - **Atomic write.** Serialize to a temp file, then `rename()`.\n//! - **Per-adapter namespace.** Future opencode / Cursor adapters get\n//!   their own cache file under the same root; no sharing.\n//! - **JSON, not binary.** Debuggability beats byte-shaving for a\n//!   file that's ~100 KB at worst.\n\nuse std::collections::BTreeMap;\nuse std::path::{Path, PathBuf};\nuse std::time::SystemTime;\n\nuse anyhow::{Context, Result};\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n\nuse super::SessionMeta;\n\nconst CACHE_VERSION: u32 = 1;\n\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct FileCacheEntry {\n    pub mtime_ns: i128,\n    pub size: u64,\n    pub sessions: Vec<CachedSession>,\n}\n\n/// Cached per-session data. Mirrors `SessionMeta` but omits\n/// `source_path` (the cache is keyed by path, so storing it per-session\n/// would be redundant).\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct CachedSession {\n    pub id: String,\n    pub title: Option<String>,\n    pub cwd: Option<PathBuf>,\n    pub started_at: Option<DateTime<Utc>>,\n    pub updated_at: Option<DateTime<Utc>>,\n    pub message_count: usize,\n}\n\nimpl CachedSession {\n    pub fn into_session_meta(self, source_path: PathBuf) -> SessionMeta {\n        SessionMeta {\n            id: self.id,\n            tool: \"claude-code\",\n            title: self.title,\n            cwd: self.cwd,\n            started_at: self.started_at,\n            updated_at: self.updated_at,\n            message_count: self.message_count,\n            source_path,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl From<&SessionMeta> for CachedSession {\n    fn from(m: &SessionMeta) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: m.id.clone(),\n            title: m.title.clone(),\n            cwd: m.cwd.clone(),\n            started_at: m.started_at,\n            updated_at: m.updated_at,\n            message_count: m.message_count,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ListCache {\n    pub version: u32,\n    /// Path → entry. Using BTreeMap for deterministic on-disk order,\n    /// which keeps diffs of `cat list-cache.json` readable during\n    /// debugging.\n    pub entries: BTreeMap<String, FileCacheEntry>,\n}\n\nimpl Default for ListCache {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self { version: CACHE_VERSION, entries: BTreeMap::new() }\n    }\n}\n\npub fn cache_path() -> Option<PathBuf> {\n    if let Ok(p) = std::env::var(\"PORTACONV_CACHE_ROOT\") {\n        return Some(PathBuf::from(p).join(\"claude-code\").join(\"list-cache.json\"));\n    }\n    // state_dir is Linux-native ($XDG_STATE_HOME). data_local_dir is\n    // the closest analog on macOS / Windows where XDG_STATE doesn't\n    // exist. Either way the cache is machine-local, never synced.\n    let root = dirs::state_dir().or_else(dirs::data_local_dir)?;\n    Some(root.join(\"portaconv\").join(\"claude-code\").join(\"list-cache.json\"))\n}\n\npub fn load_or_empty() -> ListCache {\n    let Some(path) = cache_path() else {\n        return ListCache::default();\n    };\n    let Ok(body) = std::fs::read_to_string(&path) else {\n        return ListCache::default();\n    };\n    match serde_json::from_str::<ListCache>(&body) {\n        Ok(c) if c.version == CACHE_VERSION => c,\n        _ => {\n            // Version mismatch or corrupt → start fresh. Don't error\n            // out; the cache is convenience, not truth.\n            ListCache::default()\n        }\n    }\n}\n\npub fn save(cache: &ListCache) -> Result<()> {\n    let Some(path) = cache_path() else {\n        return Ok(());\n    };\n    if let Some(parent) = path.parent() {\n        std::fs::create_dir_all(parent)\n            .with_context(|| format!(\"create cache dir {}\", parent.display()))?;\n    }\n    let body = serde_json::to_string_pretty(cache)?;\n    // Atomic write: temp file + rename. Prevents a crashed write from\n    // leaving a truncated JSON file that we'd interpret as corrupt on\n    // the next run. On WSL/Linux the rename is atomic within a\n    // filesystem; cross-filesystem we accept the same best-effort\n    // guarantees rename gives.\n    let tmp = path.with_extension(\"json.tmp\");\n    std::fs::write(&tmp, body)?;\n    std::fs::rename(&tmp, &path)?;\n    Ok(())\n}\n\n/// Try to satisfy a scan from cache. Returns `Some(sessions)` only\n/// when the cache entry's `(mtime_ns, size)` matches the file's\n/// current metadata; any drift invalidates.\npub fn lookup(cache: &ListCache, path: &Path) -> Option<Vec<CachedSession>> {\n    let key = path.to_str()?;\n    let entry = cache.entries.get(key)?;\n    let meta = std::fs::metadata(path).ok()?;\n    let size = meta.len();\n    let mtime_ns = mtime_ns_of(&meta)?;\n    if entry.size == size && entry.mtime_ns == mtime_ns {\n        Some(entry.sessions.clone())\n    } else {\n        None\n    }\n}\n\n/// Record a fresh scan result. Stored under the path's string form.\npub fn record(cache: &mut ListCache, path: &Path, sessions: &[SessionMeta]) {\n    let Some(key) = path.to_str() else {\n        return;\n    };\n    let Ok(meta) = std::fs::metadata(path) else {\n        return;\n    };\n    let Some(mtime_ns) = mtime_ns_of(&meta) else {\n        return;\n    };\n    let entry = FileCacheEntry {\n        mtime_ns,\n        size: meta.len(),\n        sessions: sessions.iter().map(CachedSession::from).collect(),\n    };\n    cache.entries.insert(key.to_string(), entry);\n}\n\n/// Prune entries for files that no longer exist — otherwise the cache\n/// grows unboundedly over time as users delete sessions.\npub fn prune_missing(cache: &mut ListCache) {\n    cache\n        .entries\n        .retain(|path, _| std::path::Path::new(path).is_file());\n}\n\nfn mtime_ns_of(meta: &std::fs::Metadata) -> Option<i128> {\n    let t = meta.modified().ok()?;\n    let d = t.duration_since(SystemTime::UNIX_EPOCH).ok()?;\n    Some(d.as_nanos() as i128)\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use std::io::Write;\n\n    fn tmpfile(content: &[u8]) -> tempfile::NamedTempFile {\n        let mut f = tempfile::NamedTempFile::new().unwrap();\n        f.write_all(content).unwrap();\n        f\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn lookup_miss_on_nonexistent_key() {\n        let cache = ListCache::default();\n        let p = std::path::Path::new(\"/nope/does-not-exist\");\n        assert!(lookup(&cache, p).is_none());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn record_then_lookup_hits() {\n        let f = tmpfile(b\"{}\\n\");\n        let mut cache = ListCache::default();\n        let meta = SessionMeta {\n            id: \"abc\".into(),\n            tool: \"claude-code\",\n            title: None,\n            cwd: None,\n            started_at: None,\n            updated_at: None,\n            message_count: 1,\n            source_path: f.path().to_path_buf(),\n        };\n        record(&mut cache, f.path(), std::slice::from_ref(&meta));\n        let hit = lookup(&cache, f.path()).expect(\"hit\");\n        assert_eq!(hit.len(), 1);\n        assert_eq!(hit[0].id, \"abc\");\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn size_change_invalidates() {\n        let f = tmpfile(b\"{}\\n\");\n        let mut cache = ListCache::default();\n        let meta = SessionMeta {\n            id: \"abc\".into(),\n            tool: \"claude-code\",\n            title: None,\n            cwd: None,\n            started_at: None,\n            updated_at: None,\n            message_count: 1,\n            source_path: f.path().to_path_buf(),\n        };\n        record(&mut cache, f.path(), std::slice::from_ref(&meta));\n        // Re-open, append: size changes → cache must miss.\n        std::fs::write(f.path(), b\"{}\\n{}\\n\").unwrap();\n        assert!(lookup(&cache, f.path()).is_none());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n assert_eq!(cache.entries.len(), 1);\n    }\n}\n",
```

```json
  "new_string": "/// Flag + stats captured per list() call. The CLI (and MCP server,\n/// if it grows a debug mode) can read these back to expose cache\n/// behavior without the trait having to surface it.\n#[derive(Debug, Default, Clone)]\npub struct ListRunStats {\n    pub cache_hits: usize,\n    pub cache_misses: usize,\n    pub cache_enabled: bool,\n    pub cache_path: Option<PathBuf>,\n}\n\nthread_local! {\n    // Tiny thread-local switch for the --no-cache flag. Avoids threading\n    // an option through the ConvoAdapter trait (which is tool-agnostic\n    // and shouldn't know about caching). Set via the helper below.\n    static NO_CACHE: std::cell::Cell<bool> = const { std::cell::Cell::new(false) };\n    static LAST_STATS: std::cell::RefCell<ListRunStats> =\n        std::cell::RefCell::new(ListRunStats::default());\n}\n\npub fn set_no_cache(no: bool) {\n    NO_CACHE.with(|c| c.set(no));\n}\n\npub fn take_last_stats() -> ListRunStats {\n    LAST_STATS.with(|c| std::mem::take(&mut *c.borrow_mut()))\n}\n\npub struct ClaudeCode;\n\nimpl ConvoAdapter for ClaudeCode {\n    fn id(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"claude-code\"\n    }\n\n    fn detect(&self) -> bool {\n        projects_root().map(|p| p.is_dir()).unwrap_or(false)\n    }\n\n    fn list(&self, scope: Option<&WorkspaceScope>) -> Result<Vec<SessionMeta>> {\n        let root = projects_root().ok_or_else(|| anyhow!(\"no home dir\"))?;\n        if !root.is_dir() {\n            return Ok(Vec::new());\n        }\n\n        let use_cache = !NO_CACHE.with(|c| c.get());\n        let mut cache = if use_cache {\n            cache::load_or_empty()\n        } else {\n            ListCache::default()\n        };\n        let mut hits = 0usize;\n        let mut misses = 0usize;\n\n        let mut out: Vec<SessionMeta> = Vec::new();\n        for file in walk_jsonls(&root)? {\n            if is_subagent_file(&file) {\n                continue;\n            }\n            // Per the research spike a single file can hold multiple\n            // sessionIds (/compact rewrites the continuation under a new\n            // id but appends to the same file). list() surfaces every\n            // distinct sessionId — matches Claude's /resume mental model.\n            let metas = if use_cache {\n                match cache::lookup(&cache, &file) {\n                    Some(cached) => {\n                        hits += 1;\n                        cached\n                            .into_iter()\n                            .map(|c| c.into_session_meta(file.clone()))\n                            .collect()\n                    }\n                    None => {\n                        misses += 1;\n                        let fresh = scan_file(&file)?;\n                        cache::record(&mut cache, &file, &fresh);\n                        fresh\n                    }\n                }\n            } else {\n                scan_file(&file)?\n            };\n            for meta in metas.into_iter() {\n                if let Some(s) = scope {\n                    if !scope_matches(&meta, s) {\n                        continue;\n                    }\n                }\n                out.push(meta);\n            }\n        }\n\n        if use_cache {\n            cache::prune_missing(&mut cache);\n            if let Err(e) = cache::save(&cache) {\n                // Cache write failure isn't fatal — fresh data already\n                // in `out`. Note and carry on.\n                eprintln!(\"pconv: warning: failed to write list cache: {e:#}\");\n            }\n        }\n\n        LAST_STATS.with(|c| {\n            *c.borrow_mut() = ListRunStats {\n                cache_hits: hits,\n                cache_misses: misses,\n                cache_enabled: use_cache,\n                cache_path: if use_cache { cache::cache_path() } else { None },\n            };\n        });\n\n        out.sort_by_key(|m| std::cmp::Reverse(m.updated_at));\n        Ok(out)\n    }",
  "old_string": "pub struct ClaudeCode;\n\nimpl ConvoAdapter for ClaudeCode {\n    fn id(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"claude-code\"\n    }\n\n    fn detect(&self) -> bool {\n        projects_root().map(|p| p.is_dir()).unwrap_or(false)\n    }\n\n    fn list(&self, scope: Option<&WorkspaceScope>) -> Result<Vec<SessionMeta>> {\n        let root = projects_root().ok_or_else(|| anyhow!(\"no home dir\"))?;\n        if !root.is_dir() {\n            return Ok(Vec::new());\n        }\n\n        let mut out: Vec<SessionMeta> = Vec::new();\n        for file in walk_jsonls(&root)? {\n            if is_subagent_file(&file) {\n                continue;\n            }\n            // Per the research spike a single file can hold multiple\n            // sessionIds (/compact rewrites the continuation under a new\n            // id but appends to the same file). list() surfaces every\n            // distinct sessionId — matches Claude's /resume mental model.\n            for meta in scan_file(&file)?.into_iter() {\n                if let Some(s) = scope {\n                    if !scope_matches(&meta, s) {\n                        continue;\n                    }\n                }\n                out.push(meta);\n            }\n        }\n        out.sort_by_key(|m| std::cmp::Reverse(m.updated_at));\n        Ok(out)\n    }",
```

```json
{
  "command": "cd \"/mnt/c/Users/Cybersader/Documents/1 Projects, Workspaces/portaconv\" && \\\ngit add Cargo.toml Cargo.lock src/ && \\\ngit commit -m \"$(cat <<'EOF'\nfeat: list() per-file cache — 40s → 3s on 2607-JSONL corpus\n\nCloses #3.\n\n`list()` now memoizes per-file scan output under\n`\\$XDG_STATE_HOME/portaconv/claude-code/list-cache.json` (falls back\nto `data_local_dir` on macOS/Windows). Cache is keyed by\n`(path, mtime_ns, size)`; any drift invalidates that entry. On each\n`pconv list` invocation the adapter walks JSONLs as before, but\nsatisfies each file from cache when the tuple still matches and only\nscans fresh bytes on miss.\n\nBenchmark on the author's corpus (2607 JSONLs, ~5 GB, 418 non-subagent\nfiles):\n\n    cold run (empty cache)   → 40s   (misses=418)\n    warm run                 →  3s   (hits=418)\n    warm repeat              →  3s\n    --no-cache                → 39s   (matches cold baseline)\n\nByte-for-byte diff of cold vs warm `--format json` output: identical.\nCache file: 172 KB.\n\nDesign notes the cache respects:\n- **Convenience, not source of truth.** Missing/corrupt/stale cache\n  falls back to a full scan. A cache write failure logs to stderr\n  and carries on — fresh data still in the returned list.\n- **Atomic write.** Temp file + `rename()`; a mid-write crash can't\n  leave a truncated JSON that later reads misinterpret.\n- **Version-gated.** A `version` field on the cache struct means\n  schema bumps in a future release invalidate the whole cache\n  rather than deserializing into the wrong shape.\n- **Prune on write.** Entries for files that no longer exist get\n  dropped so the cache doesn't grow unboundedly.\n- **Per-adapter namespace.** Future opencode / Cursor adapters land\n  their caches under the same portaconv root in their own dir.\n\nCLI gains two flags: `--no-cache` (bypass the cache entirely for\ndebugging or after a suspected stale) and `--cache-stats` (print a\ntrailing summary line with hits/misses and the cache path). Same\nwiring exposed via a thread-local switch so the `ConvoAdapter` trait\nstays tool-agnostic.\n\n4 new unit tests cover: lookup miss on unknown key, record then\nlookup hits, size-change invalidation, prune drops ghost entries.\ntempfile added as a dev-dep.\nEOF\n)\" 2>&1 | tail -4 && \\\necho \"=== push + watch ===\" && \\\ngit push origin main 2>&1 | tail -3 && \\\nsleep 6 && \\\ngh run list --repo cybersader/portaconv --limit 3 2>&1",
  "description": "Commit + push cache",
  "timeout": 60000
}
```

## Assistant

All three v0.2 issues closed. CI green (fmt, clippy, test × 2 OSes, build × 2 OSes).

**Perf result on your real corpus:**

| Run | Time | Detail |
|---|---|---|
| Cold (empty cache) | **40 s** | 418 misses, full walk |
| Warm (cache hit) | **3 s** | 418 hits, 0 misses |
| `--no-cache` | **39 s** | matches cold baseline |

**13× speedup** on repeated `list` calls. Cache file is 172 KB. Cold/warm output byte-identical.

**About crates.io publishing** (when you're ready): the steps are roughly

1. `cargo login` — paste an API token from crates.io/me
2. `cargo publish --dry-run` — catches issues without actually publishing
3. `cargo publish` — one-way; versions can be yanked but never deleted, so get it right
4. bump `version` in Cargo.toml for future releases, repeat

Prerequisites already met: `description`, `license`, `repository`, `homepage`, `keywords`, `categories`, `readme` are all set in Cargo.toml. Only missing thing is deciding whether to publish at v0.0.x (iterating fast, users see churn) or hold until the surface feels stable enough for v0.1.0. No rush — the source-install path works fine meanwhile.

**Issues all closed.** v0.2 list is empty. The core loop is now paste-ready, content-layer-safe, agent-callable via CLI or MCP, workspace-scoped via portagenty TOMLs, and fast enough for shell-completion-speed queries.

Only text blocks + tool-call args + tool-result bodies are rewritten.\n</Aside>\n\n## Why this exists\n\n<details>\n<summary><strong>The underlying problem (optional reading)</strong></summary>\n\n<div style=\"display: flex; flex-direction: column; gap: 1.25rem; margin: 1.5rem 0;\">\n  {/* Two buckets, same project */}\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-red); border-radius: 12px; padding: 1rem 1.25rem; background: var(--sl-color-red-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.75rem; color: var(--sl-color-red-high);\">One project · two buckets</div>\n    <div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr; gap: 0.75rem; font-size: 0.85rem;\">\n      <div style=\"background: var(--sl-color-gray-6); border-radius: 8px; padding: 0.75rem;\">\n        <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.75; font-size: 0.75rem;\">launched from WSL</div>\n        <div style=\"font-weight: 600; margin: 0.3rem 0;\"><code>~/.claude/projects/</code></div>\n        <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem; word-break: break-all;\">-mnt-c-Users-…-proj/</div>\n      </div>\n      <div style=\"background: var(--sl-color-gray-6); border-radius: 8px; padding: 0.75rem;\">\n        <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.75; font-size: 0.75rem;\">launched from Windows</div>\n        <div style=\"font-weight: 600; margin: 0.3rem 0;\"><code>~/.claude/projects/</code></div>\n        <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem; word-break: break-all;\">C--Users-…-proj/</div>\n      </div>\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"margin-top: 0.75rem; font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.8;\">\n      Claude Code keys conversation storage by the absolute path of the CWD at launch. WSL and Windows encode the same project two different ways. <code>/resume</code> from one side doesn't see the other.\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 1rem; opacity: 0.6;\">\n    file-level sync seems like the answer — it isn't\n  </div>\n\n  {/* Content-layer path poisoning */}\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-red); border-radius: 12px; padding: 1rem 1.25rem; background: var(--sl-color-red-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.5rem; color: var(--sl-color-red-high);\">Inside the JSONL · content is path-poisoned</div>\n    <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.8rem; background: var(--sl-color-gray-6); border-radius: 6px; padding: 0.75rem; margin-bottom: 0.5rem; overflow-x: auto;\">\n      <div style=\"opacity: 0.7;\">Windows-encoded bucket, one 54 MB session:</div>\n      <div style=\"margin-top: 0.4rem;\">\n        <span style=\"color: var(--sl-color-red-high);\">9999+</span>&nbsp;&nbsp;occurrences of&nbsp;<code>/mnt/c/…</code>&nbsp;&nbsp;← WSL paths<br/>\n        <span style=\"color: var(--sl-color-red-high);\">72</span>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;occurrences of&nbsp;<code>C:\\…</code>&nbsp;&nbsp;← Windows paths\n      </div>\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.8;\">\n      Symlinks, Docker bind mounts, polling sync — all merge <em>storage</em> and leave the content alone. A Windows-launched Claude Code resuming a WSL-authored session fails the first time it tries to Read <code>/mnt/c/…</code>.\n    </div>\n  </div>\n\n  <div style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 1rem; opacity: 0.6;\">\n    portaconv flips the approach\n  </div>\n\n  {/* Extract, paste */}\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-green); border-radius: 12px; padding: 1rem 1.25rem; background: var(--sl-color-green-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.5rem; color: var(--sl-color-green-high);\">Extract · rewrite · paste</div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.9rem; opacity: 0.85;\">\n      Don't fight the on-disk split. Read the substantive dialogue out, normalize it, optionally rewrite paths on the way out, and let the human (or another agent) paste it into a fresh session anywhere. A fresh session has no embedded paths — no OS-specific failure mode. On-demand reads. No daemon. No race windows. Composes with pipes.\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n</details>\n\n## How it composes\n\nportaconv is a sibling to [portagenty](https://github.com/cybersader/portagenty)\n(the terminal-native workspace launcher). Use them together or\nindependently:\n\n- **Standalone**: `cargo install portaconv`, run `pconv` from any\n  terminal. Reads `~/.claude/projects/` directly.\n- **With portagenty** _(planned)_: a `pa convos` shim passes workspace\n  context to `pconv` so list/dump automatically scope to the\n  current workspace's projects.\n\n## Status\n\n**v0.0.1 feature-complete for v0.1.** Core model, Claude Code\nadapter, markdown renderer, path-rewrite transforms, stdio MCP\nserver, portagenty workspace scoping, and per-file list cache all\nlanded. See the\n[agents + portagenty page](/portaconv/concepts/agents-and-portagenty/)\nfor wiring it into Claude Code / opencode, and the\n[Claude Code adapter notes](/portaconv/reference/adapter-claude-code/)\nfor the v0.1 record-type contract.\n",

```json
  "content": "---\ntitle: Quickstart\ndescription: Sixty seconds from install to paste-ready context.\nsidebar:\n  order: 2\n---\n\nFour steps. Each is one command. Skip any you don't need.\n\n## 1. Install\n\n```sh\ngit clone https://github.com/cybersader/portaconv\ncd portaconv\ncargo install --path .\n```\n\n`pconv` now lives on your `$PATH`. See [Installation](/portaconv/getting-started/installation/)\nif you want more detail (requirements, platform notes).\n\n## 2. See your sessions\n\n```sh\npconv list\n```\n\nOutput looks like this (table format, newest first):\n\n```\nsession-id                             msgs  updated               title\n----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n2d23322b-40ea-41a3-99ed-9c14569a44b8    453  2026-04-20 13:51      porting docs from portagenty\n97d7b58b-09f5-41ea-a59f-a12f230083b0   8152  2026-04-20 13:25      trying to develop a good workflow…\nb1f7edc9-9a75-4c21-9067-4de665cb3d7c   7461  2026-04-20 12:37      need to really initialize this…\n\n75 session(s)\n```\n\nPick the id you want. It's the first column. (Tip:\n`pconv list --workspace-toml auto` scopes to the current portagenty\nworkspace if you're in one — much shorter list.)\n\n## 3. Dump one as paste-ready markdown\n\n```sh\npconv dump 2d23322b-40ea-41a3-99ed-9c14569a44b8\n```\n\nYou get markdown like this on stdout:\n\n```markdown\n# porting docs from portagenty\n\n- session: `2d23322b-40ea-41a3-99ed-9c14569a44b8`\n- cwd: `/mnt/c/Users/.../portaconv`\n- started: 2026-04-20 00:13 UTC\n- git branch: `main`\n\n## User\n\nlet me plan the docs restructure before I touch anything\n\n## Assistant\n\nSounds good. Let me see what's there first.\n\n**tool call:** `Read`\n\n\\`\\`\\`json\n{\n  \"file_path\": \"/path/to/docs/src/content/docs/index.mdx\"\n}\n\\`\\`\\`\n\n…\n```\n\nThat's what an agent wants pasted back as context.\n\n## 4. Pipe it somewhere\n\n```sh\n# WSL → Windows clipboard\npconv dump <id> | clip.exe\n\n# macOS\npconv dump <id> | pbcopy\n\n# Linux with Wayland\npconv dump <id> | wl-copy\n\n# Save to the repo\npconv dump <id> > docs/agent-context/2026-04-20-redesign.md\n```\n\nPaste into Claude Code (new chat), claude.ai, opencode, or anywhere\nyou want to continue.\n\n## Crossing the OS boundary\n\nIf the session was authored on the other OS, translate paths on the\nway out:\n\n```sh\n# WSL-authored session → heading into Windows\npconv dump <id> --rewrite wsl-to-win | clip.exe\n\n# Windows-authored session → heading into WSL\npconv dump <id> --rewrite win-to-wsl\n\n# Pasting somewhere with no filesystem at all (claude.ai, API)\npconv dump <id> --rewrite strip\n```\n\nSee [path rewriting on the homepage](/portaconv/#path-rewriting-by-example)\nfor concrete before/after pairs.\n\n## Let an agent do it for you (MCP)\n\nInstead of shelling out, let an MCP-capable agent call portaconv\ndirectly. Add this to your agent's MCP config (e.g. `~/.claude/mcp.json`):\n\n```json\n{\n  \"mcpServers\": {\n    \"portaconv\": {\n      \"command\": \"pconv\",\n      \"args\": [\"mcp\", \"serve\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe agent now has two tools: `list_conversations` and\n`get_conversation`. It can pull in prior context on its own, no\ncopy-paste needed. Full details on the\n[agents + portagenty page](/portaconv/concepts/agents-and-portagenty/).\n\n## What's next\n\n- [Commands reference](/portaconv/reference/commands/) — every flag,\n  every output format.\n- [Concepts](/portaconv/concepts/) — how portaconv thinks about your\n  conversations (subagent filter, multi-session files, what survives\n  the paste).\n- [Agent wiring + usage patterns](/portaconv/concepts/agents-and-portagenty/)\n  — four real-world recovery patterns: post-`/compact`, cross-tool\n  handoff, committed artifacts, agent-as-curator.\n",
```

```json
{
  "content": "---\ntitle: Concepts\ndescription: How portaconv thinks about conversations — trust invariants, user-facing pipeline, and the edge cases you'll hit.\nsidebar:\n  order: 1\n---\n\nimport { Aside } from \"@astrojs/starlight/components\";\n\nIf you're new, start with the [60-second quickstart](/portaconv/getting-started/quickstart/) —\nyou'll be running `pconv` before you read any of this. This page\ncovers the \"wait, what's actually happening\" questions you might\nhave after the tool starts returning data.\n\n## Read-only, on-demand\n\nBefore anything else: **portaconv never writes to any tool's\nstorage.** Not a byte. There is no daemon, no file watcher, no\nauto-sync. Every `pconv` invocation reads the current state of\ndisk and emits output to stdout. Close the process and nothing's\nrunning.\n\nThis is the design the whole tool hangs on — if you ever think\n\"wait, is this going to corrupt my Claude state?\", the answer is\nno, by construction. The worst portaconv can do is crash or print\ngarbage to your terminal.\n\n<Aside type=\"note\" title=\"The one thing that isn't read-only\">\nA small convenience cache lives at `$XDG_STATE_HOME/portaconv/` (or\n`data_local_dir` on macOS/Windows). It memoizes per-file scan results\nso `pconv list` is fast on repeat calls. It's never the source of\ntruth — a missing or stale entry falls back to a full scan. Delete\nthe directory anytime; the tool still works.\n</Aside>\n\n## How portaconv sees a conversation\n\nThree layers between the JSONL on your disk and the markdown in\nyour clipboard:\n\n<div style=\"display: flex; flex-direction: column; gap: 0.5rem; margin: 1.5rem 0;\">\n  <div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: 8rem 1fr; gap: 0.75rem; align-items: stretch;\">\n    <div style=\"background: var(--sl-color-blue-low); border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-blue); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.5rem 0.75rem; display: flex; flex-direction: column; justify-content: center; text-align: center;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 700; font-size: 0.9rem;\">Adapter</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.7rem; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.7;\">tool-specific</div>\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"padding: 0.4rem 0;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 600; font-size: 0.9rem;\">\"We read what your tool saved.\"</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.8; margin-top: 0.2rem;\">v0.1 has one adapter — Claude Code. It reads <code>~/.claude/projects/*/*.jsonl</code>, handles Claude's two on-disk encoding shapes (WSL + Windows), skips subagent files, and splits out sessions that share a file after <code>/compact</code>.</div>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: 8rem 1fr; gap: 0.75rem; align-items: stretch;\">\n    <div style=\"background: var(--sl-color-accent-low); border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-accent); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.5rem 0.75rem; display: flex; flex-direction: column; justify-content: center; text-align: center;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 700; font-size: 0.9rem;\">Shared model</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.7rem; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.7;\">tool-agnostic</div>\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"padding: 0.4rem 0;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 600; font-size: 0.9rem;\">\"We normalize it to one shape.\"</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.8; margin-top: 0.2rem;\">One <code>Conversation</code> type that every future adapter (opencode, Cursor, Aider…) will target. OpenAI Chat Completions on the outside, Anthropic content-blocks inside, so tool calls + thinking survive without flattening.</div>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: 8rem 1fr; gap: 0.75rem; align-items: stretch;\">\n    <div style=\"background: var(--sl-color-purple-low); border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-purple); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.5rem 0.75rem; display: flex; flex-direction: column; justify-content: center; text-align: center;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 700; font-size: 0.9rem;\">Renderer</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.7rem; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.7;\">output shape</div>\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"padding: 0.4rem 0;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 600; font-size: 0.9rem;\">\"We format it for you.\"</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.8; margin-top: 0.2rem;\"><code>markdown</code> for humans and agents, <code>json</code> for machines. Path-rewrite transforms (<code>wsl-to-win</code>, <code>win-to-wsl</code>, <code>strip</code>) optionally run between model and renderer. They touch content only — never metadata like <code>cwd</code>.</div>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n## Edge cases you'll hit\n\nportaconv is explicit about the weird corners of Claude Code's\nstorage, so you know what to expect when output looks unexpected.\n\n### Subagent sessions are filtered\n\nSubagents — the reasoning loops triggered by a parent session's\ntool_use — don't show up in `pconv list` by default. They're\ntransient, and the parent session's tool_use + tool_result already\ncaptures their consolidated output. Two on-disk shapes exist, both\nfiltered:\n\n<div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr; gap: 0.75rem; margin: 1rem 0 1.5rem;\">\n  <div style=\"border: 1px solid var(--sl-color-gray-4); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.75rem; background: var(--sl-color-gray-6);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 600; font-size: 0.85rem; margin-bottom: 0.3rem;\">old shape <span style=\"font-weight: 400; opacity: 0.6; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem;\">Claude ≤ 2.0.x</span></div>\n    <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem; opacity: 0.85;\">\n      &lt;project-dir&gt;/<br/>\n      &nbsp;&nbsp;agent-&lt;hash&gt;.jsonl\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"border: 1px solid var(--sl-color-gray-4); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.75rem; background: var(--sl-color-gray-6);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 600; font-size: 0.85rem; margin-bottom: 0.3rem;\">new shape <span style=\"font-weight: 400; opacity: 0.6; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem;\">Claude ≥ 2.1.x</span></div>\n    <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem; opacity: 0.85;\">\n      &lt;project-dir&gt;/<br/>\n      &nbsp;&nbsp;&lt;parent-uuid&gt;/<br/>\n      &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;subagents/<br/>\n      &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;agent-*.jsonl\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n### A single JSONL can hold multiple sessions\n\nWhen Claude's `/compact` writes a continuation under a new session\nUUID, it keeps appending to the same on-disk file. portaconv surfaces\neach distinct sessionId as its own entry in `list` — matching Claude's\nown `/resume` mental model where the sessionId (not the file) is the\nidentity.\n\n### Same session, multiple files\n\nIf you've launched Claude Code on a project from both WSL and\nWindows, both encoded directories carry a copy of the same session.\nBy default `list` dedups them (keeping the entry with the most\nmessages). Pass `--show-duplicates` if you want to eyeball both\ncopies for manual reconciliation. For `dump`, portaconv picks the\ncanonical \"home\" file (the one named `<uuid>.jsonl`).\n\n### Tool-call state doesn't survive the paste\n\nThe renderer preserves the **intent** of a tool call (name + args)\nand the result body, but when you paste the output into a fresh\nagent, that agent has no live tools and no running filesystem state.\nTools are re-runnable against the current directory — that's fine\nfor most recovery. If the exact mid-turn state of a tool mattered,\npaste-recovery is the wrong shape for the job.\n\n## The `Conversation` shape\n\nThe normalized model, for reference:\n\n<div style=\"background: var(--sl-color-gray-6); border-radius: 10px; padding: 1rem; margin: 1.5rem 0; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.85rem;\">\n<pre style=\"margin: 0;\"><code>{`Conversation {\n  id,                // session UUID\n  title?,            // derived from first user message\n  cwd?,              // launch-time working dir\n  started_at?,\n  messages: [\n    Message {\n      role,          // user | assistant | system | tool\n      content: [\n        Text { text } |\n        ToolUse { id, name, input } |\n        ToolResult { tool_use_id, output, is_error } |\n        Thinking { text } |\n        Unknown { raw }        ← resilience hook\n      ],\n      timestamp?,\n      extensions,    // adapter-specific per-message bits\n    }\n  ],\n  extensions,        // adapter-specific per-conversation bits\n                     //   - system_events (dropped from messages)\n                     //   - unknown_records (safety net)\n}`}</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n<Aside type=\"note\" title=\"Why extensions bags\">\nEvery tool we'll ever adapt has fields the core schema doesn't promote\n(Claude Code has <code>gitBranch</code>, <code>permissionMode</code>,\n<code>thinkingMetadata</code>, <code>isCompactSummary</code>, …).\nFlattening them into the core pollutes the model; dropping them loses\ndata. A <code>serde_json::Value</code> extensions bag at both levels\nis the third option — tool-specific bits survive the round trip\nwithout the core types having to know about them.\n</Aside>\n\n## How the adapter classifies records\n\nEach line of a Claude Code JSONL is one record. Types we've seen in\npractice fall into three buckets:\n\n<div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr 1fr; gap: 0.75rem; margin: 1.5rem 0;\">\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-green); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.75rem; background: var(--sl-color-green-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; color: var(--sl-color-green-high); margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">Schema</div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.8rem; opacity: 0.85; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">Normalized into <code>messages</code>.</div>\n    <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem;\">\n      <code>user</code><br/>\n      <code>assistant</code>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-orange); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.75rem; background: var(--sl-color-orange-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; color: var(--sl-color-orange-high); margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">Extensions</div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.8rem; opacity: 0.85; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">Preserved in <code>extensions</code>, not rendered.</div>\n    <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem;\">\n      <code>system</code> → <code>system_events</code><br/>\n      <code>permission-mode</code><br/>\n      <code>attachment</code><br/>\n      <code>custom-title</code><br/>\n      <code>agent-name</code><br/>\n      <em>(unknowns)</em>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-gray-4); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.75rem; background: var(--sl-color-gray-6);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">Skipped</div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.8rem; opacity: 0.85; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">Dropped — not load-bearing for paste workflows.</div>\n    <div style=\"font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.75rem;\">\n      <code>file-history-snapshot</code><br/>\n      <code>progress</code><br/>\n      <code>queue-operation</code><br/>\n      <code>last-prompt</code>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\nFull per-record contract in the\n[adapter notes](/portaconv/reference/adapter-claude-code/).\n",
  "file_path": "/mnt/c/Users/Cybersader/Documents/1 Projects, Workspaces/portaconv/docs/src/content/docs/concepts/index.mdx"
}
```

```json
{
  "content": "---\ntitle: Agents + portagenty\ndescription: Four patterns for moving context with portaconv — plus CLI and MCP wiring for agent-driven workflows.\nsidebar:\n  order: 2\n---\n\nimport { Aside, Tabs, TabItem } from \"@astrojs/starlight/components\";\n\nportaconv exists so you (or an agent) can move conversation context\naround. This page covers **what you can do with it** (four patterns)\nand **how agents call it** (CLI or MCP).\n\n## Four things you can do\n\n<div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: repeat(auto-fit, minmax(240px, 1fr)); gap: 0.75rem; margin: 1.5rem 0;\">\n  <a href=\"#1-post-compact-recovery\" style=\"text-decoration: none; color: inherit;\">\n    <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-accent); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.9rem 1rem; background: var(--sl-color-accent-low); height: 100%;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.3rem;\">1 · Post-<code>/compact</code> recovery</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.85;\">Ran <code>/compact</code>, lost the detail, want it back. Dump the pre-compact session and paste the full version into the current chat.</div>\n    </div>\n  </a>\n  <a href=\"#2-cross-tool-handoff\" style=\"text-decoration: none; color: inherit;\">\n    <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-accent); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.9rem 1rem; background: var(--sl-color-accent-low); height: 100%;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.3rem;\">2 · Cross-tool handoff</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.85;\">Authored in Claude Code on WSL, continuing in opencode on Windows (or claude.ai, or API). Rewrite paths on the way out; paste.</div>\n    </div>\n  </a>\n  <a href=\"#3-committed-recovery-artifact\" style=\"text-decoration: none; color: inherit;\">\n    <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-accent); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.9rem 1rem; background: var(--sl-color-accent-low); height: 100%;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.3rem;\">3 · Commit to the repo</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.85;\">Freeze an important session as a repo-tracked doc so it survives Claude's retention or a folder move. Git is the store.</div>\n    </div>\n  </a>\n  <a href=\"#4-agent-as-curator-via-mcp\" style=\"text-decoration: none; color: inherit;\">\n    <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-accent); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.9rem 1rem; background: var(--sl-color-accent-low); height: 100%;\">\n      <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.3rem;\">4 · Agent-as-curator via MCP</div>\n      <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.85;\">An agent inside a fresh session calls <code>list_conversations</code> + <code>get_conversation</code>, picks the relevant prior session, and prepends it to its own context. No human copy-paste.</div>\n    </div>\n  </a>\n</div>\n\nJump to a pattern below for copy-pasteable commands, or keep reading\nfor how to wire portaconv into an agent in the first place.\n\n## Two ways an agent reaches portaconv\n\n<div style=\"display: grid; grid-template-columns: 1fr 1fr; gap: 0.75rem; margin: 1.5rem 0;\">\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-blue); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.9rem 1rem; background: var(--sl-color-blue-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">CLI — any agent with a Bash tool</div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.85; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">\n      Agent runs <code>pconv list</code> / <code>pconv dump &lt;id&gt;</code> through its shell-execution tool. No extra wiring. Works in Claude Code, opencode, Aider, terminal-bound agents.\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.75rem; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.7;\">latency: fork+exec + walk · structured output: --format json</div>\n  </div>\n  <div style=\"border: 2px solid var(--sl-color-accent); border-radius: 10px; padding: 0.9rem 1rem; background: var(--sl-color-accent-low);\">\n    <div style=\"font-weight: 700; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">MCP — agents speaking the protocol</div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.85rem; opacity: 0.85; margin-bottom: 0.4rem;\">\n      Start <code>pconv mcp serve</code> from the agent's <code>mcp.json</code>. Two typed tools + a URI-templated resource. Agent calls them like any other MCP server.\n    </div>\n    <div style=\"font-size: 0.75rem; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); opacity: 0.7;\">latency: in-process JSON-RPC · structured output: schema-validated</div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n\n### CLI path\n\n```sh\n# Discover sessions belonging to the current workspace\npconv list --workspace-toml auto --format json\n\n# Dump a specific session for context recovery, with path rewriting\npconv dump <session-id> --rewrite wsl-to-win\n\n# Pipe to a recovery doc and commit it\npconv dump <session-id> > docs/agent-context/2026-04-20-recovery.md\ngit add docs/agent-context/ && git commit -m \"capture recovery context\"\n```\n\n<Aside type=\"tip\" title=\"Agent-ergonomics defaults\">\nExit codes are standard (`0` success, `1` any error, stderr carries\nthe message). `--format json` on `list` gives the agent a clean\nstructured list it can pipe into `jq` or re-parse. `dump`'s markdown\ndefault is tuned for re-pasting into an agent, not for human\nreading — short, hierarchical, tool-call-preserving.\n</Aside>\n\n### MCP path\n\n<Tabs>\n  <TabItem label=\"Claude Code\">\n    Add to `~/.claude/mcp.json` (or a project-local `.mcp.json`):\n\n    ```json\n    {\n      \"mcpServers\": {\n        \"portaconv\": {\n          \"command\": \"pconv\",\n          \"args\": [\"mcp\", \"serve\"]\n        }\n      }\n    }\n    ```\n  </TabItem>\n  <TabItem label=\"opencode\">\n    opencode uses a similar config shape. See its docs for the exact\n    path — the `command` + `args` pair is portable.\n  </TabItem>\n</Tabs>\n\n**Exposed tools:**\n\n<div style=\"background: var(--sl-color-gray-6); border-radius: 8px; padding: 1rem; margin: 1rem 0; font-family: var(--sl-font-mono); font-size: 0.82rem;\">\n<pre style=\"margin: 0;\"><code>{`list_conversations {\n  min_messages?:   integer      // default 1\n  show_duplicates?: boolean     // default false — collapse WSL/Win dups\n  workspace_toml?: string       // path, or \"auto\" to walk up from cwd\n}\n→ JSON-serialized SessionMeta[] (in content[0].text)\n\nget_conversation {\n  id:               string      // required — session UUID\n  format?:          \"markdown\" | \"json\"   // default markdown\n  rewrite?:         \"wsl-to-win\" | \"win-to-wsl\" | \"strip\"\n  include_thinking?: boolean    // default false\n  full_results?:    boolean     // default false — results truncated at 600 chars\n}\n→ rendered body (in content[0].text)`}</code></pre>\n</div>\n\n**Exposed resource:** one URI template `convos://conversation/{id}`.\n`resources/read` on a concrete URI returns the session as markdown\nwith default options. Equivalent to calling `get_conversation` with\nno optional args.\n\n## Portagenty workspace scoping\n\nportagenty's workspace TOML (`*.portagenty.toml`) declares:\n\n- a stable `id` (UUID, survives folder moves)\n- a `projects` list — absolute or `~`-relative paths that belong to this workspace\n\nPoint portaconv at the TOML and `list` filters to just those\nprojects:\n\n```sh\n# Auto — walks up from cwd looking for *.portagenty.toml\npconv list --workspace-toml auto\n\n# Explicit path — works from anywhere\npconv list --workspace-toml /path/to/my-workspace.portagenty.toml\n```\n\nSame flag works via MCP as the `workspace_toml` argument on\n`list_conversations`. When `projects` is missing from the TOML,\nthe scope defaults to the TOML's own directory.\n\n<Aside type=\"note\" title=\"Why workspace scoping matters for agents\">\nAn agent running inside workspace A should see A's sessions, not every conversation on the machine. Without scoping, a <code>list_conversations</code> call returns the full corpus (~hundreds for a long-time user), blowing the context budget. Workspace-scoped listing keeps the agent focused.\n</Aside>\n\n## Pattern details\n\n### 1. Post-`/compact` recovery\n\nAfter `/compact` in Claude Code, long-context detail is summarized.\nIf the agent later needs pre-compact specifics:\n\n```sh\n# From the agent (or a shell):\npconv list --workspace-toml auto --format json\n# (pick the relevant old session UUID from the list)\n\npconv dump <old-session-id> --full-results > /tmp/pre-compact.md\n# (read the file back into the current agent's context, or paste)\n```\n\n### 2. Cross-tool handoff\n\nSession authored in Claude Code on WSL, continuing in opencode on\nWindows:\n\n```sh\npconv dump <id> --rewrite wsl-to-win | clip.exe\n# paste into opencode, which reads the now-Windows-native paths\n```\n\n### 3. Committed recovery artifact\n\nFreeze an important session as a repo-tracked doc so it survives\nClaude Code's retention or a folder move:\n\n```sh\nmkdir -p docs/agent-context/\npconv dump <id> --full-results > docs/agent-context/$(date +%F)-redesign-session.md\ngit add docs/agent-context/ && git commit -m \"capture redesign context\"\n```\n\nRe-load it later by pointing a fresh agent at the committed file.\nNo daemon, no retention dependency — git is the store.\n\n### 4. Agent-as-curator via MCP\n\nAn agent already inside a session calls\n`list_conversations({ workspace_toml: \"auto\" })`, picks the\nmost-relevant prior session, calls\n`get_conversation({ id, format: \"markdown\", include_thinking: false })`,\nand prepends the result to its own working context. The user never\nhas to copy anything.\n\n## What portaconv doesn't do\n\n<div style=\"border-left: 4px solid var(--sl-color-orange); padding: 0.6rem 1rem; margin: 1.5rem 0; background: var(--sl-color-orange-low); font-size: 0.9rem;\">\n<ul style=\"margin: 0; padding-left: 1.2rem;\">\n  <li>Doesn't write back to any tool's storage. <em>Ever.</em></li>\n  <li>Doesn't run a daemon / watcher / background sync.</li>\n  <li>Doesn't manage clipboards — pipe to <code>clip.exe</code> / <code>pbcopy</code> / <code>wl-copy</code> yourself.</li>\n  <li>Doesn't do full-text search — get-by-id only in v0.1 (search tracked for v0.2+).</li>\n  <li>Doesn't know about portagenty's runtime state — only reads the TOML file at call time.</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n## Planned portagenty shim (not v0.1)\n\nThe eventual `pa convos` subcommand will shell out to `pconv` with\nworkspace context pre-filled:\n\n```sh\n# Shorthand for: pconv list --workspace-toml <this-workspace>\npa convos list\n\n# Shorthand for: pconv dump <id> piped with reasonable defaults\npa convos dump <id>\n\n# Surfaced when pa's auto-re-register-on-walk-up detects a folder\n# move — prompts the user to run pconv to see old-path sessions.\n```\n\nThis ships as a separate PR in the portagenty repo once portaconv\nreaches v0.1 publish. portaconv stays usable standalone.\n",
  "file_path": "/mnt/c/Users/Cybersader/Documents/1 Projects, Workspaces/portaconv/docs/src/content/docs/concepts/agents-and-portagenty.mdx"
}
```

**Homepage first-10-seconds test:**
