## User

Thinking from the context-engineering perspective.  If agents are potentially using this or people (interactively sometimes in terminal), then does this tool account for that.  For instance, can you use search terms in the commands (is that a good or bad idea - loaded can of worms?), can you sort by a certain column in that list?  Would things like that be valuable?

## Assistant

## Assistant

Good sharp question. The current tool half-accounts for this. Let me split the answer into "what's genuinely valuable" vs "can of worms":

## Current state

`pconv list` today has: `--format`, `--min-messages`, `--show-duplicates`, `--workspace-toml`, `--no-cache`. Default sort is `updated` descending. Agents pipe `--format json | jq ...` for anything custom. Humans eyeball the table. It's thin — lots of use cases force people into jq or "scroll and squint".

## What's cheap and clearly valuable

Four additions are low-cost and immediately useful to both audiences:

| Flag | Human use | Agent use |
|---|---|---|
| `--since <dur>` (e.g., `2d`, `7d`, `2026-04-01`) | "where's yesterday's work" | "only pull last-week's context" |
| `--sort <key>` (updated / started / msgs / title / id), `--reverse` | "show me the chatty ones" | deterministic ordering for reproducibility |
| `--limit N` (after filter/sort) | "top 5" | bounded MCP response size |
| `--grep <substr>` on title+cwd, case-insensitive | "the react refactor one" | cheap typed filter |

Adding the cwd column to the table output also pays off — cwd is often how you recognize a session, more than the title (which gets derived from whatever you typed first, often `<local-command-caveat>` noise).

**Every one of these should mirror in MCP** as typed arguments on `list_conversations`. That's the real context-engineering win: the agent's schema tells it what it can filter on. Right now the schema only advertises `min_messages / show_duplicates / workspace_toml` — an agent wanting "sessions from last 2 days about tests" has no typed path, so it calls the broad tool and pulls the whole corpus into its context.

## The can of worms

**Full-content search** (match against message bodies, not just title/cwd). Genuinely different:
- Needs an index (tokenize, store, invalidate on mtime)
- Has to decide: just text blocks? tool_use args? tool_results too?
- Relevance ranking?
- Stemming / fuzzy?

The pattern in the broader ecosystem is `grep` / `ripgrep`-style (exact, fast, streaming) vs `pagefind` / FTS (indexed, relevance-scored). For portaconv, the extract-not-sync philosophy argues against maintaining an index — the cache is already the one stateful compromise.

**My take:** `--grep` against title + cwd is substring and trivially cheap (both are already in SessionMeta). Full-content search stays v0.2+ and should live as a separate verb (`pconv search <query>`) with clear semantics, not bolted into `list`.

**Fuzzy matching** (nucleo / fzf-style) is nice but adds a dep and UX expectations (ranking, highlighting). Defer until someone asks.

## What I'd propose to build

Tier A — the four filters above + cwd column + MCP parity. Maybe 200 LOC + tests. Tight enough to ship as one commit.

Tier B (separate follow-up, next session or later):
- `pconv search <query>` — full-content substring grep, streams through JSONLs (no index)
- Later: optional index + relevance, when there's enough user signal to justify it

Want me to build Tier A now? Or want to push on any of the design choices first (e.g., "sort keys should be X", "skip `--grep`, agents have jq", "add cwd column but not the rest")?

## User

yeah let's avoid going too deep with deps or can of worms problems.  If however this somehow maps to the protagenty philosophies and workspace type stuff, then good.  Just make sure docs have properly communicated eveyrhting

## Assistant

## Assistant

Good — Tier A stays dep-free (chrono is already in; everything else is std). The portagenty mapping is lean: we already have `--workspace-toml auto`, new filters compose cleanly on top, no new coupling needed. I'll make sure the docs land the "these compose with workspace scope" story.

Scope lock:

- `--since <dur>` — `2d`/`7d`/`24h`/`30m` or ISO date (`2026-04-01`)
- `--sort <key>` + `--reverse` — updated/started/msgs/title/id
- `--limit N`
- `--grep <substr>` — case-insensitive title+cwd substring (NOT full-content; that's v0.2 `pconv search`)
- `cwd` column in table output
- Full MCP parity on `list_conversations`
- Docs updates on commands/quickstart/agents/index

Zero new deps. One commit. Executing.

  "new_string": "/// Collapse duplicate `SessionMeta` entries with the same id, keeping the\n/// one with the highest `message_count` (tie-break: most recent\n/// `updated_at`). Same sessionId shows up multiple times when a project\n/// has been launched from both WSL and Windows — the two encoded-dir\n/// buckets each carry a copy. Callers that want the raw multi-entry\n/// view skip this step.\npub fn dedup_sessions(mut metas: Vec<SessionMeta>) -> Vec<SessionMeta> {\n    use std::collections::HashMap;\n    let mut best: HashMap<String, SessionMeta> = HashMap::new();\n    for m in metas.drain(..) {\n        match best.get(&m.id) {\n            Some(existing)\n                if (existing.message_count, existing.updated_at)\n                    >= (m.message_count, m.updated_at) => {}\n            _ => {\n                best.insert(m.id.clone(), m);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    let mut out: Vec<SessionMeta> = best.into_values().collect();\n    out.sort_by_key(|m| std::cmp::Reverse(m.updated_at));\n    out\n}\n\n/// Sort key for `sort_sessions`. Default across the app is `Updated`\n/// descending — matches what humans expect when glancing at a \"recent\n/// sessions\" list.\n#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub enum SortKey {\n    Updated,\n    Started,\n    Msgs,\n    Title,\n    Id,\n}\n\npub fn sort_sessions(metas: &mut [SessionMeta], key: SortKey, reverse: bool) {\n    // Stable sort so equal keys keep their relative order from the\n    // caller (typically still walk-order, which preserves predictability).\n    match key {\n        SortKey::Updated => metas.sort_by_key(|m| m.updated_at),\n        SortKey::Started => metas.sort_by_key(|m| m.started_at),\n        SortKey::Msgs => metas.sort_by_key(|m| m.message_count),\n        SortKey::Title => {\n            metas.sort_by(|a, b| a.title.as_deref().cmp(&b.title.as_deref()))\n        }\n        SortKey::Id => metas.sort_by(|a, b| a.id.cmp(&b.id)),\n    }\n    // Default semantics:\n    //   updated/started/msgs → newest/biggest first (reverse-of-ascending)\n    //   title/id             → alphabetic ascending\n    // `reverse` flips whichever default applies.\n    let default_descending = matches!(\n        key,\n        SortKey::Updated | SortKey::Started | SortKey::Msgs\n    );\n    if default_descending ^ reverse {\n        metas.reverse();\n    }\n}\n\n/// Cap a session list after filtering/sorting. `0` means no cap.\npub fn limit_sessions(metas: Vec<SessionMeta>, limit: usize) -> Vec<SessionMeta> {\n    if limit == 0 || metas.len() <= limit {\n        metas\n    } else {\n        metas.into_iter().take(limit).collect()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Case-insensitive substring match on title + cwd. Intentionally NOT\n/// full-content search — that's a separate verb we'd add later with\n/// proper streaming and no index. This is the cheap discovery filter\n/// humans and agents reach for first: \"the react refactor one\",\n/// \"anything under /mnt/c/work/api\".\npub fn grep_sessions(metas: Vec<SessionMeta>, needle: &str) -> Vec<SessionMeta> {\n    if needle.is_empty() {\n        return metas;\n    }\n    let n = needle.to_lowercase();\n    metas\n        .into_iter()\n        .filter(|m| {\n            let title_hit = m\n                .title\n                .as_deref()\n                .map(|t| t.to_lowercase().contains(&n))\n                .unwrap_or(false);\n            let cwd_hit = m\n                .cwd\n                .as_ref()\n                .and_then(|p| p.to_str())\n                .map(|p| p.to_lowercase().contains(&n))\n                .unwrap_or(false);\n            title_hit || cwd_hit\n        })\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Parse a `--since` value into an absolute `DateTime<Utc>` threshold.\n///\n/// Accepted shapes, tried in order:\n///   - relative:   `30m`, `6h`, `2d`, `4w`\n///   - RFC 3339:   `2026-04-01T12:00:00Z`\n///   - ISO date:   `2026-04-01` (interpreted as 00:00 UTC on that day)\n///\n/// Zero new deps — `chrono::Duration` + `NaiveDate::parse_from_str`\n/// cover everything.\npub fn parse_since(s: &str) -> Result<DateTime<Utc>> {\n    let s = s.trim();\n    if s.is_empty() {\n        return Err(anyhow!(\"--since: empty value\"));\n    }\n\n    // Relative form: trailing m / h / d / w, rest is a positive integer.\n    if let Some(last) = s.chars().last() {\n        if matches!(last, 'm' | 'h' | 'd' | 'w') {\n            let body = &s[..s.len() - 1];\n            if let Ok(n) = body.parse::<i64>() {\n                if n <= 0 {\n                    return Err(anyhow!(\"--since: duration must be positive (got {s})\"));\n                }\n                let delta = match last {\n                    'm' => chrono::Duration::minutes(n),\n                    'h' => chrono::Duration::hours(n),\n                    'd' => chrono::Duration::days(n),\n                    'w' => chrono::Duration::weeks(n),\n                    _ => unreachable!(),\n                };\n                return Ok(Utc::now() - delta);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Absolute: RFC 3339 first (carries timezone), then date-only.\n    if let Ok(dt) = DateTime::parse_from_rfc3339(s) {\n        return Ok(dt.with_timezone(&Utc));\n    }\n    if let Ok(d) = NaiveDate::parse_from_str(s, \"%Y-%m-%d\") {\n        let dt = d\n            .and_hms_opt(0, 0, 0)\n            .ok_or_else(|| anyhow!(\"--since: invalid date {s}\"))?;\n        return Ok(DateTime::<Utc>::from_naive_utc_and_offset(dt, Utc));\n    }\n\n    Err(anyhow!(\n        \"--since: can't parse {s:?} — expected a duration like `2d` or a date like `2026-04-01`\"\n    ))\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    fn meta(id: &str, msgs: usize, updated_iso: Option<&str>) -> SessionMeta {\n        SessionMeta {\n            id: id.into(),\n            tool: \"claude-code\",\n            title: None,\n            cwd: None,\n            started_at: None,\n            updated_at: updated_iso\n                .and_then(|s| DateTime::parse_from_rfc3339(s).ok())\n                .map(|d| d.with_timezone(&Utc)),\n            message_count: msgs,\n            source_path: std::path::PathBuf::new(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn parse_since_relative_shapes() {\n        let now = Utc::now();\n        let two_days = parse_since(\"2d\").unwrap();\n        assert!(now - two_days > chrono::Duration::hours(47));\n        assert!(now - two_days < chrono::Duration::hours(49));\n\n        assert!(parse_since(\"30m\").is_ok());\n        assert!(parse_since(\"6h\").is_ok());\n        assert!(parse_since(\"4w\").is_ok());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn parse_since_absolute_date() {\n        let got = parse_since(\"2026-04-01\").unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(got.format(\"%Y-%m-%d\").to_string(), \"2026-04-01\");\n        assert_eq!(got.format(\"%H:%M:%S\").to_string(), \"00:00:00\");\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn parse_since_rfc3339() {\n        assert!(parse_since(\"2026-04-01T12:00:00Z\").is_ok());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn parse_since_rejects_garbage() {\n        assert!(parse_since(\"\").is_err());\n        assert!(parse_since(\"banana\").is_err());\n        assert!(parse_since(\"0d\").is_err());\n        assert!(parse_since(\"-1d\").is_err());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn sort_by_msgs_desc_by_default() {\n        let mut v = vec![\n            meta(\"a\", 1, None),\n            meta(\"b\", 10, None),\n            meta(\"c\", 5, None),\n        ];\n        sort_sessions(&mut v, SortKey::Msgs, false);\n        assert_eq!(v[0].id, \"b\");\n        assert_eq!(v[1].id, \"c\");\n        assert_eq!(v[2].id, \"a\");\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn sort_reverse_flips() {\n        let mut v = vec![\n            meta(\"a\", 1, None),\n            meta(\"b\", 10, None),\n            meta(\"c\", 5, None),\n        ];\n        sort_sessions(&mut v, SortKey::Msgs, true);\n        assert_eq!(v[0].id, \"a\");\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn sort_title_ascending_by_default() {\n        let mut v = vec![\n            SessionMeta { title: Some(\"charlie\".into()), ..meta(\"1\", 0, None) },\n            SessionMeta { title: Some(\"alpha\".into()), ..meta(\"2\", 0, None) },\n            SessionMeta { title: Some(\"bravo\".into()), ..meta(\"3\", 0, None) },\n        ];\n        sort_sessions(&mut v, SortKey::Title, false);\n        assert_eq!(v[0].title.as_deref(), Some(\"alpha\"));\n        assert_eq!(v[2].title.as_deref(), Some(\"charlie\"));\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn limit_caps_output() {\n        let v = vec![meta(\"a\", 0, None), meta(\"b\", 0, None), meta(\"c\", 0, None)];\n        assert_eq!(limit_sessions(v.clone(), 0).len(), 3); // 0 = unlimited\n        assert_eq!(limit_sessions(v.clone(), 2).len(), 2);\n        assert_eq!(limit_sessions(v, 99).len(), 3);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn grep_matches_title_or_cwd_case_insensitive() {\n        let v = vec![\n            SessionMeta {\n                title: Some(\"React refactor\".into()),\n                cwd: Some(\"/work/api\".into()),\n                ..meta(\"a\", 0, None)\n            },\n            SessionMeta {\n                title: Some(\"misc notes\".into()),\n                cwd: Some(\"/work/frontend\".into()),\n                ..meta(\"b\", 0, None)\n            },\n            SessionMeta {\n                title: None,\n                cwd: Some(\"/home/x\".into()),\n                ..meta(\"c\", 0, None)\n            },\n        ];\n        let hit = grep_sessions(v.clone(), \"react\");\n        assert_eq!(hit.len(), 1);\n        assert_eq!(hit[0].id, \"a\");\n\n        let hit = grep_sessions(v.clone(), \"work\");\n        assert_eq!(hit.len(), 2); // matched via cwd\n\n        let hit = grep_sessions(v.clone(), \"\");\n        assert_eq!(hit.len(), 3); // empty needle = passthrough\n    }\n}",

Errors if neither is usable.\nfn resolve_dump_target(adapter: &ClaudeCode, args: &DumpArgs) -> Result<String> {\n    if let Some(id) = args.session_id.as_deref() {\n        if args.latest {\n            return Err(anyhow!(\n                \"--latest and a positional session id are mutually exclusive — pick one\"\n            ));\n        }\n        return Ok(id.to_string());\n    }\n    if !args.latest {\n        return Err(anyhow!(\n            \"pconv dump: give a session id, or pass --latest (optionally with --workspace-toml auto)\"\n        ));\n    }\n    let scope = build_workspace_scope(args.workspace_toml.as_deref())?;\n    let metas = adapter\n        .list(Some(&scope))\n        .context(\"listing sessions to resolve --latest\")?;\n    let metas = dedup_sessions(metas);\n    // adapter.list already sorts updated_at desc; after dedup the\n    // first entry is the freshest surviving session.\n    let pick = metas.into_iter().next().ok_or_else(|| {\n        anyhow!(\n            \"no sessions found{}\",\n            if args.workspace_toml.is_some() {\n                \" in this workspace\"\n            } else {\n                \"\"\n            }\n        )\n    })?;\n    Ok(pick.id)\n}\n\n/// Truncate a path-ish string to a visual width, keeping the useful\n/// tail (projects are recognizable by their last segments, not their\n/// `/home/cybersader/…` prefix).\nfn truncate_middle(s: &str, width: usize) -> String {\n    if s.chars().count() <= width {\n        return s.to_string();\n    }\n    // \"…\" + last (width - 1) chars.\n    let tail: String = s.chars().rev().take(width - 1).collect();\n    let tail: String = tail.chars().rev().collect();\n    format!(\"…{tail}\")\n}",

Clients\n    // parse this themselves — the schema here matches the convention\n    // used by other MCP servers.\n    let payload = serde_json::to_string(&metas).map_err(|e| (-32603, format!(\"serialize: {e}\")))?;\n    Ok(json!({\n        \"content\": [ { \"type\": \"text\", \"text\": payload } ]\n    }))\n}\n\nfn parse_sort_key(s: Option<&str>) -> Result<SortKey, String> {\n    match s.unwrap_or(\"updated\") {\n        \"updated\" => Ok(SortKey::Updated),\n        \"started\" => Ok(SortKey::Started),\n        \"msgs\" => Ok(SortKey::Msgs),\n        \"title\" => Ok(SortKey::Title),\n        \"id\" => Ok(SortKey::Id),\n        other => Err(format!(\"unknown sort key: {other}\")),\n    }\n}",

Surfaces each\ndistinct sessionId — a single JSONL may hold several when `/compact`\nwrites a continuation to the same file.\n\n```sh\npconv list                                  # table (default), newest first\npconv list --format json\npconv list --min-messages 5                 # hide short placeholder sessions\npconv list --workspace-toml auto            # scope to current portagenty workspace\npconv list --show-duplicates                # keep WSL- + Windows-encoded copies\n```\n\n### Filtering, sorting, limiting\n\n```sh\n# Time window — relative or absolute\npconv list --since 2d                       # last 2 days\npconv list --since 6h\npconv list --since 2026-04-01               # from a date\n\n# Substring search on title + cwd (NOT full content)\npconv list --grep react\npconv list --grep /work/api\n\n# Sort by column; use --reverse to flip direction\npconv list --sort msgs                      # chattiest first\npconv list --sort title                     # A → Z\npconv list --sort started --reverse         # oldest first\n\n# Cap output\npconv list --limit 10\n\n# Compose: last week, containing \"refactor\", in the current workspace, top 5\npconv list --workspace-toml auto --since 7d --grep refactor --limit 5\n```\n\n**Sort keys:** `updated` (default), `started`, `msgs`, `title`, `id`.\nTime and count keys default to newest/biggest first; `title` and `id`\ndefault to ascending alphabetic. `--reverse` flips whichever default\napplies.\n\n**Output columns (table):** `session-id · msgs · updated · cwd · title`.\nTitle is derived from the first user message; cwd is truncated with a\nleading `…` when long (the project's tail is usually more\nrecognizable than its home-dir prefix).\n\nSubagent JSONLs are filtered by path pattern and do not appear in\nthe list — see the\n[concepts page](/portaconv/concepts/#subagent-sessions-are-filtered)\nfor the rule.",

## Assistant

## Assistant

Honest answer: **no — it doesn't exist today.** `pconv dump` renders the full session. The only size-capping knobs are per-block: `--full-results` toggles tool-result truncation, and thinking blocks hide by default. Neither slices the conversation overall.

That's a real gap for paste workflows (both human "just give me the tail" and agent context-budget use). Adding `--tail N` now — simple, no deps, keeps the most-recent N messages and notes how many were dropped. Mirroring in MCP.

}

  "new_string": "impl ContentBlock {\n    pub fn text(s: impl Into<String>) -> Self {\n        Self::Text { text: s.into() }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Conversation {\n    /// Keep only the last `tail` messages. Records a `truncated` entry\n    /// in `extensions` so downstream consumers (markdown renderer, JSON\n    /// readers) can surface that the paste is a slice, not the whole\n    /// thing. A `tail` of `0` is a no-op. If the session already has\n    /// ≤ `tail` messages the whole conversation is preserved untouched.\n    pub fn apply_tail(&mut self, tail: usize) {\n        if tail == 0 || self.messages.len() <= tail {\n            return;\n        }\n        let original = self.messages.len();\n        let dropped = original - tail;\n        self.messages = self.messages.split_off(dropped);\n\n        let mut ext_map = self\n            .extensions\n            .as_object()\n            .cloned()\n            .unwrap_or_else(serde_json::Map::new);\n        ext_map.insert(\n            \"truncated\".into(),\n            serde_json::json!({\n                \"tail\": tail,\n                \"original_message_count\": original,\n                \"dropped\": dropped,\n            }),\n        );\n        self.extensions = Value::Object(ext_map);\n    }\n}",

  "file_path": "/mnt/c/Users/Cybersader/Documents/1 Projects, Workspaces/portaconv/docs/src/content/docs/concepts/index.mdx",
  "new_string": "## What you can rely on\n\nBefore anything else: **portaconv never writes to any tool's\nstorage.** Not a byte. There is no daemon, no file watcher, no\nauto-sync. Every `pconv` invocation reads the current state of\ndisk and emits output to stdout. Close the process and nothing's\nrunning.\n\nIf you ever wonder \"is this going to corrupt my Claude state?\",\nthe answer is no, by construction. The worst portaconv can do is\ncrash or print garbage to your terminal.\n\nThat's the foundational invariant. The rest of the system is\nlayered on top with explicit reliability tiers — worth knowing\nif you're automating against the tool.\n\n### Reliability tiers\n\n<div style=\"overflow-x: auto; margin: 1.25rem 0;\">\n<table style=\"width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse; font-size: 0.85rem;\">\n  <thead>\n    <tr style=\"background: var(--sl-color-gray-6);\">\n      <th style=\"text-align: left; padding: 0.5rem; border-bottom: 2px solid var(--sl-color-gray-4);\">Layer</th>\n      <th style=\"text-align: left; padding: 0.5rem; border-bottom: 2px solid var(--sl-color-gray-4); color: var(--sl-color-green-high);\">Always the same</th>\n      <th style=\"text-align: left; padding: 0.5rem; border-bottom: 2px solid var(--sl-color-gray-4); color: var(--sl-color-blue-high);\">Opt-in (off by default)</th>\n      <th style=\"text-align: left; padding: 0.5rem; border-bottom: 2px solid var(--sl-color-gray-4); color: var(--sl-color-orange-high);\">Could drift</th>\n    </tr>\n  </thead>\n  <tbody>\n    <tr>\n      <td style=\"padding: 0.6rem 0.5rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--sl-color-gray-5); font-weight: 600;\">Read path</td>\n      <td style=\"padding: 0.6rem 0.5rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--sl-color-gray-5);\">Read-only; stdio-only output; cache miss always falls back to full scan.</td>\n      <td style=\"padding: 0.6rem 0.5rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--sl-color-gray-5);\"><code>--no-cache</code> bypasses cache entirely.</td>\n      <td style=\"padding: 0.6rem 0.5rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--sl-color-gray-5);\">Claude Code on-disk format — new record types get captured in <code>extensions.unknown_records</code>, never silently dropped.</td>\n    </tr>\n    <tr>\n      <td style=\"padding: 0.6rem 0.5rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--sl-color-gray-5); font-weight: 600;\">Normalization</td>\n      <td style=\"padding: 0.6rem 0.5rem; border-bottom: 1px solid var(--sl-color-gray-5);\">OpenAI outer + Anthropic inner content-blocks. Delete anytime; no data loss.</td>\n    </tr>\n  </tbody>\n</table>\n</div>\n\n### What paste does NOT preserve\n\n<div style=\"border-left: 4px solid var(--sl-color-orange); padding: 0.6rem 1rem; margin: 1.5rem 0; background: var(--sl-color-orange-low); font-size: 0.9rem;\">\n<p style=\"margin: 0 0 0.5rem 0;\"><strong>Lossy by design</strong> — don't expect any of these to survive:</p>\n<ul style=\"margin: 0; padding-left: 1.2rem;\">\n  <li><strong>Tool-call runtime state.</strong> The new agent has no running tools and no live file state. Tool <em>args</em> and <em>results</em> survive; the actual live process does not.</li>\n  <li><strong>Subagent internal reasoning.</strong> Filtered out at the adapter layer. The parent session's <code>tool_use</code> + <code>tool_result</code> already carries the consolidated output.</li>\n  <li><strong>Internal Claude metadata records</strong> — <code>file-history-snapshot</code>, <code>progress</code>, <code>queue-operation</code> are dropped (they're not part of the conversation's substance).</li>\n  <li><strong>Conversation identity across paste.</strong> You're starting a new session in the new tool; the sessionId changes. portaconv preserves the <em>content</em>, not the identity.</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n### Predictability checklist\n\nIf you're scripting against portaconv, these are safe assumptions:\n\n- Same JSONL bytes + same flags → same output bytes (within the same pconv version).\n- `--format json` is a stable contract at the field level; extensions may gain fields but won't rename or drop core ones.\n- Exit codes: `0` success, non-zero any error, `stderr` carries the message.\n- `--grep` never matches message content — only title and cwd. \"Full-content search\" stays a separate verb if/when it lands.\n- `--tail N` on a session with fewer than N messages is a no-op (no spurious truncation marker).",
  "old_string": "## Read-only, on-demand\n\nBefore anything else: **portaconv never writes to any tool's\nstorage.** Not a byte. There is no daemon, no file watcher, no\nauto-sync. Every `pconv` invocation reads the current state of\ndisk and emits output to stdout. Close the process and nothing's\nrunning.\n\nThis is the design the whole tool hangs on — if you ever think\n\"wait, is this going to corrupt my Claude state?\", the answer is\nno, by construction. The worst portaconv can do is crash or print\ngarbage to your terminal.\n\n<Aside type=\"note\" title=\"The one thing that isn't read-only\">\nA small convenience cache lives at `$XDG_STATE_HOME/portaconv/` (or\n`data_local_dir` on macOS/Windows). It memoizes per-file scan results\nso `pconv list` is fast on repeat calls. It's never the source of\ntruth — a missing or stale entry falls back to a full scan. Delete\nthe directory anytime; the tool still works.\n</Aside>",
  "replace_all": false
}

## User

What's the shim?

## Assistant

## Assistant

A **shim** is a thin wrapper that sits between two things and translates. In portagenty's case: a small `pa convos` subcommand that shells out to `pconv` with workspace context pre-filled, so users don't have to type it themselves.

**Concretely, what the shim adds:**

| Without shim (today) | With shim (future) |
|---|---|
| `pconv list --workspace-toml auto` | `pa convos list` |
| `pconv dump --latest --workspace-toml auto \| clip.exe` | `pa convos last \| clip.exe` |
| `pconv dump <id> --rewrite wsl-to-win` | `pa convos dump <id> --rewrite wsl-to-win` |

Internally `pa convos list` would just do:
```rust
Command::new("pconv")
    .args(["list", "--workspace-toml", &current_workspace_toml_path])
    .status()
```

**Why it's a shim, not "integration":**
- portagenty doesn't link to portaconv as a library, doesn't know the adapter internals
- It just shells out to the `pconv` binary and adds the workspace-scope flag
- If pconv isn't installed, `pa convos` prints "install it with `cargo install portaconv`" and exits
- portaconv stays fully usable without portagenty — the shim is pure ergonomic sugar

**Why it's planned but not built:**
- Lives in the **portagenty repo**, not this one — it's portagenty's responsibility to know about its own workspace-file format
- Requires portaconv to be stable first (which it effectively is now)
- Would also surface the folder-move-recovery hint: when `pa` auto-re-registers on walk-up and detects a workspace moved, it could say "heads up, old-path conversations exist — run `pa convos list` to see them."

Small scope, small code — maybe 100 LOC in portagenty plus an install-hint. Whenever you want to cut it, it's a one-evening PR on portagenty's side.

  "content": "---\ntitle: Roadmap\ndescription: Ideas and potential features for portaconv — not commitments, explicit tiers of likelihood, and a record of what's been explicitly decided against.\nsidebar:\n  order: 1\n---\n\n:::note\nThis isn't a commitment list. It's a snapshot of where ideas sit —\nsome likely, some speculative, some explicitly parked. The goal is\nto keep design decisions visible alongside the \"what if we…\" pile\nso neither gets forgotten. Actionable items live on the\n[GitHub issue tracker](https://github.com/cybersader/portaconv/issues);\nanything here without an issue link is still idea-shaped.\n:::\n\n## Likely next\n\nThings that probably make sense once there's user signal or the\nnext 1-2 sessions of focused work.\n\n- **Additional adapters.** Aider first (plain markdown in\n  `.aider.chat.history.md`, cheapest adapter we could land);\n  opencode next (similar storage shape to Claude Code);\n  continue.dev after that. Cursor's SQLite storage is meaningfully\n  harder and waits until demand justifies it.\n- **crates.io publish** once the surface feels stable. Tag v0.1.0,\n  `cargo publish`, users install with `cargo install portaconv`\n  instead of cloning.\n- **Schema promotion for production-observed record types.** The\n  spike's initial six record types were joined by five more\n  surfaced on real corpus data (`permission-mode`, `attachment`,\n  `last-prompt`, `custom-title`, `agent-name`). Most should stay in\n  the extensions bag, but `custom-title` in particular deserves\n  promotion to `Conversation.title` when present, overriding the\n  first-user-message heuristic.\n\n## Maybe (ideas worth recording, not prioritized)\n\n- **`pconv search <query>`** — a separate verb for full-content\n  search, streaming through JSONLs with no index. Deliberately\n  distinct from `list --grep` (which stays substring-over-title+cwd)\n  so the scope creep of FTS doesn't bleed into the discovery filter.\n- **`pconv copy <id>`** — bake in clipboard support with OS\n  auto-detection (`clip.exe`, `pbcopy`, `wl-copy`, `xclip`). Removes\n  the `| clip.exe` pipe dance. Small win; currently piping works.\n- **`pconv export --to <file>`** — shorthand for `pconv dump <id> >\n  <file>`. Arguably sugar; `>` already works.\n- **Fuzzy-matched `list --find`** — nucleo-ranked (same crate\n  portagenty uses) for \"kinda remember the project name\" flows. The\n  dep is real weight though; punt unless someone asks.\n- **Snapshot tests for markdown renderer** — `insta` is already a\n  dev-dep and unused. Lock down the rendered shape so format\n  regressions surface on PR diff.\n- **Property tests for path-rewrite edge cases** — paths with\n  spaces, UNC paths, paths adjacent to URLs. Catch the subtle\n  regex cases my hand-rolled tests miss.\n- **Cache warm-up on first install** — the first `pconv list` on a\n  big corpus is 40s; subsequent runs are 3s. A `pconv cache warm`\n  subcommand that pre-fills in the background would make the first\n  interactive call feel instant.\n- **Shell completions** — `pconv completions bash|zsh|fish` emits\n  a completion script. clap makes this trivial; hold until someone\n  hits a dead-end tab-completing `--sort`.\n\n## Portagenty-side (lives in the other repo)\n\nThese ideas **aren't portaconv's to build** — they'd ship as PRs\non [portagenty](https://github.com/cybersader/portagenty). The\nreceiving-side contract (what flags pconv accepts, what output\nformat it emits) is settled and documented here; the consumer is\nupstream.\n\n- **`pa convos` shim.** Small wrapper that shells out to `pconv`\n  with workspace context pre-filled. `pa convos list` →\n  `pconv list --workspace-toml <current>`. `pa convos last` →\n  `pconv dump --latest --workspace-toml <current>`. If pconv isn't\n  installed, print an install hint and exit. ~100 LOC + an install\n  check.\n- **Folder-move recovery hint.** pa's auto-re-register-on-walk-up\n  already detects when a workspace file shows up at a new path.\n  When it does, emit a status line: \"heads up — old-path\n  conversations may still exist; run `pconv list --workspace-id\n  <uuid>` to see them.\" Would need portaconv to accept\n  `--workspace-id <uuid>` and resolve it against portagenty's\n  workspace registry — meaningful coupling, defer unless someone\n  actually hits the scenario.\n- **`pa://convos/<workspace-id>`** protocol-handler route. pa\n  already registers a `pa://` URL scheme for cross-device deep\n  links; this slot would resolve to `pconv list` filtered to that\n  workspace. Nice-to-have, low demand.\n\n## Won't do (design decisions, recorded so nobody re-argues them)\n\nThese are parked permanently unless the foundation shifts. The\nanswers below came from the original design Q&A and live in\n[`knowledgebase/03-design-decisions.md`](https://github.com/cybersader/portaconv/blob/main/knowledgebase/03-design-decisions.md).\n\n- **Interactive TUI viewer.** Different niche. jhlee0409's\n  [claude-code-history-viewer](https://github.com/jhlee0409/claude-code-history-viewer)\n  covers browsing well; portaconv stays CLI-pipe-friendly.\n- **Daemon / file watcher / auto-sync.** The whole thesis is\n  extract-on-demand, not continuous-sync. A daemon brings back\n  every problem the research doc catalogued (race windows,\n  divergence, content-layer poisoning). Non-starter.\n- **Writes to any tool's storage.** Read-only by construction.\n  Every feature is additive; not one byte goes back to\n  `~/.claude/projects/`.\n- **FTS bolted into `--grep`.** `--grep` is substring-over-title-\n  and-cwd and stays that way. Full-content search is a **separate**\n  verb (see \"Maybe\") if / when it lands.\n- **`pconv import`** or any flow that writes markdown back into a\n  tool's native format. If you want to commit context, use\n  `pconv dump <id> > docs/agent-context/whatever.md` and git-add\n  it. Git is the store.\n\n## What's already shipped\n\nFor context — the following are done and live:\n\n- Core schema + Claude Code adapter\n- `list` + `dump` (markdown/json) + `mcp serve`\n- Path-rewrite transforms (`wsl-to-win`, `win-to-wsl`, `strip`)\n- Tier A list filters (`--since` / `--sort` / `--reverse` /\n  `--limit` / `--grep`)\n- `dump --latest --workspace-toml auto` one-liner\n- `dump --tail N` length control with self-documenting truncation\n- Full MCP schema parity (every CLI flag mirrored as a tool argument)\n- Per-file list cache (~13× speedup on 2607-JSONL corpus)\n- v0.2 issues #1 #2 #3 all closed\n\nIf something here looks like it should be on a different tier,\nopen an [issue](https://github.com/cybersader/portaconv/issues) and\nargue for it.\n",

## On your portagenty question

Short answer: **you don't need to switch workspaces just to discuss the idea.** The split is:

| Kind of question | Where to have it |
|---|---|
| "What flags / schema should portaconv expose so `pa convos` is possible?" | Here, in portaconv. It's the *receiving-side contract*. Already settled — `--workspace-toml` exists, MCP mirrors it, all good. |
| "Does it make sense to build `pa convos` at all? What should the CLI shape be?" | Either place works, but the roadmap page acknowledges the idea as-park-but-not-our-build. |
| "Actually writing the `pa convos` subcommand / wiring it into the TUI" | **Portagenty workspace.** That's where `pa`'s source lives. When you're ready to implement, you'd switch over there. |

The roadmap page makes this split explicit — anything under "Portagenty-side" is labeled as "lives in the other repo" so a future contributor reading the roadmap here doesn't start a PR in the wrong place.

## Full stack now live

```
c9f2801 docs: roadmap page — potential features, tiered by likelihood
7c8f59a docs: agent-ergonomic restructure + reliability tiers + schema refresh
1ddd039 feat: list filters + dump --latest/--tail + MCP parity
2f60a78 feat: list() per-file cache — 40s → 3s on 2607-JSONL corpus
…
```

Site: 10/10 smoke routes, 9 content pages, zero open v0.2 issues. Ready for the next direction.

## User

What's the workflow problem i originally had in mind here btw?

## Assistant

## Assistant

The specific incident from the bootstrap knowledgebase (`01-challenge-source.md` — "Recovery Story, 2026-04-19"):

You were running the `claudecode-project-sync` Docker container to bridge WSL ↔ Windows Claude Code dirs. Then `/resume` from WSL started showing you **conversations from 2 months ago** instead of the session you'd been in the night before. Investigation turned up:

- **6 encoded directories** for one project in `~/.claude/projects/` (same-project copies under `-mnt-c-…` and `C--…` encodings, plus sub-path variants)
- The two live 54 MB buckets held the same session UUID but had **silently diverged by ~20 KB** within the same day (Docker sync had lost the race)
- Spot-check of one JSONL: **9999+ `/mnt/c/…` + 72 `C:\…`** paths baked into content — proof that *file-level sync can't fix content-level poisoning*

That was the trigger. The broader workflow problem it pointed at:

| Your symptom | Root cause |
|---|---|
| `/resume` shows stale sessions | Claude Code keys storage by CWD string; WSL/Windows encode the same project two ways |
| Sync daemon silently diverges | Race window between polling intervals; bi-directional conflict |
| Even if you merged storage, the content still has wrong-OS paths | Content-layer poisoning — `Read /mnt/c/…` fails on Windows no matter which dir it lives in |
| No way to resume across different tools at all | Every agent stores history in its own format; no lingua franca |
| `/compact` detail loss, retention wipes, folder moves | Conversation history is fragile and machine-local |

The pivot you articulated: **stop trying to make sessions resume in place. Extract the substance and let it paste into any fresh session anywhere.** Fresh sessions have no embedded paths → no OS failure mode; work on-demand → no race windows; compose with pipes → no daemon.

That's what portaconv turned into. Every feature we've built maps back to a facet of that original workflow pain:

- `pconv list/dump` — see and extract sessions without resuming them
- `--rewrite wsl-to-win | win-to-wsl | strip` — the direct fix for content-layer path poisoning
- `--workspace-toml auto` + dedup — clean up the 6-dir mess you found
- `--tail N` — paste just what matters after `/compact` loss
- MCP + `--latest` — let agents pull yesterday's context automatically
- Committed recovery artifacts pattern — git as the store when retention isn't

Want me to pull that framing into a "Why this exists" preamble on the roadmap page or somewhere else prominent? Could anchor the docs to the original incident with a date + link to the upstream issues (#17682, #9668, #9306) for people hitting the same thing.

## User

I meant the reason I want more integration with portagenty - how smooth could I make it?

## Assistant

## Assistant

Ah. Missed the target there — the workflow problem isn't the path-poisoning incident, it's the broader **portable-agent-workspace** frustration that motivates wanting pa and pconv to feel like one thing.

## The workflow you're chasing (my read)

portagenty already makes the *terminal* portable: `pa claim` from your phone and the desktop session reshapes to your screen. Sessions live in tmux/zellij on the server; the terminal attached to them changes. You can walk between laptop → desktop → phone over SSH and the environment just follows.

But the **conversations** don't ride along. The multiplexer carries the live process; it doesn't carry what the agent was thinking, or the running context of a different session you had yesterday on a different tool. Concretely:

- You `pa claim` a workspace on a new device → the attached Claude Code session is the same one (good), but there's no way for it to see *other* sessions that happened in this workspace before.
- Walk away from your laptop, come back tomorrow on your desktop, `pa` into the same workspace → Claude Code sees only *this machine's* `~/.claude/projects/`. Yesterday's laptop session is stranded.
- After `/compact`, context is lost; you have to manually remember "oh I had a long session last week with the answer."
- You move a project folder → pa re-registers fine, but your old conversations are tied to the old encoded-dir.

**The unified picture:** a workspace is a *portable context surface*. Right now portagenty makes the terminal portable; portaconv could make the conversation history portable. Together they'd mean: open a workspace from any device → immediately have both a running session AND the ability to reach into the workspace's conversation history, scoped + filtered for you.

## Tiers of "how smooth"

### Cheap ergonomics — one portagenty PR each

- **`pa convos list` / `pa convos last`** — the shim I described. Zero new capability, just removes typing. `pa convos last` = "dump the most recent session in this workspace."
- **`pa claim` adds a pointer**, not a paste. On attach, print a footer line: "this workspace has 8 prior Claude sessions; `pa convos last` to resume the newest." Doesn't inject context automatically (that burns tokens); just tells you it's available.
- **Folder-move recovery hint.** pa already auto-re-registers on walk-up; when it detects an id-move, append: "old-path sessions may exist — `pa convos list --workspace-id <uuid>` to bridge them."

### Mid-weight — small schema change on both sides

- **`pa init` writes an `.mcp.json`** in the workspace dir with the `portaconv` MCP server pre-configured. Then any Claude Code session launched by `pa` inside that workspace has `list_conversations` / `get_conversation` available *with no per-session setup*. Agents can reach back into workspace history as a native capability, not a bolt-on.
- **Context-budget-aware commands.** `pa convos last --safe` → uses `pconv dump --latest --tail 80` so the paste definitely fits; "safe" meaning "fits in a default context window."
- **`pa://convos/<workspace-id>`** deep link. Tap it on your phone → opens the workspace TUI scrolled to the conversation view. Works because pa already has the `pa://` scheme registered.

### Cross-device, the ambitious part

- **pconv lives on the server, not the client.** You `pa claim` from your phone into the desktop's zellij session; that session's Claude Code process has MCP access to the desktop's pconv (which sees the desktop's full `~/.claude/projects/`). No install on the phone. The phone is a terminal, period. This is probably the single biggest unlock and it *already works today* — you just haven't felt it yet because you'd have to be inside a pa-managed session with MCP wired up.
- **Cross-workspace pinning.** "When I launch workspace A, always surface sessions tagged with `@setup` at the top." Would need a small `pa` config field.
- **Auto-commit-on-important.** When pa detects "this session is getting long / critical," offer to dump it into the workspace's `docs/agent-context/`. Git becomes the durable store the way the workspace TOML already is for config.

### Probably not worth it

- pa running pconv as a background daemon. Violates portaconv's extract-on-demand design. Not needed — pa's `pa claim` already provides the "I'm here now" moment to run pconv fresh.
- pa owning session identity / merging multiple Claude sessions into one abstract "workspace conversation." Conversations are discrete events; merging loses more than it gives.

## The answer to "how smooth"

**About as smooth as tmux + ssh already is**, if we take the mid-weight tier seriously. A workspace becomes: a portable TOML + a session picker (the pa TUI) + a native MCP capability (pconv) that any agent launched in the workspace can reach. The user never types `pconv` directly unless they want to; the agent does it for them via MCP; `pa convos` is the human-friendly shim.

Want me to add a "Workflow vision" section to the roadmap page capturing this? Or to `knowledgebase/` where the other design-intent docs live? The "portable-agent-workspace" framing feels load-bearing enough that it deserves a written home — it's the thing that ties portagenty and portaconv together into one story.

The issue is that I can't really easily do that from within something like a zellij session to say "get this workspace's portaconv history - or maybe i can i guess since it's related to the CWD or whatever portagenty toml is available. ## Assistant

## Assistant

Got it — two separate things tangled together:

## How the TOML actually maps to portaconv

The `id` field isn't involved (yet). The mapping is purely through **paths**:

```toml
name = "portaconv"
id   = "76452e59-..."              # not read by pconv (reserved for future)
projects = [
  "~/code/portaconv",              # these paths get used
  "~/code/portagenty"              # absolute or ~-expanded
]
```

When you run `pconv list --workspace-toml auto`:

1. Walks up from cwd looking for any `*.portagenty.toml`
2. Parses the `projects` list (or falls back to the TOML's own dir if missing)
3. Walks every JSONL under `~/.claude/projects/`
4. Keeps only sessions whose **stored `cwd` field** (recorded in each record at launch time) starts with one of those project paths
5. Returns that filtered set

So it's: *TOML declares which directory-prefixes count as "this workspace"; pconv uses those prefixes to filter Claude's path-keyed storage.* No registry, no id lookup, no coupling.

## The in-session friction is real but solvable today

You're right that copying stuff out of Claude Code to paste back in is awful. But Claude Code can already reach into the shell *without leaving the session*. Three ways, ordered by friction:

### 1. `!` prefix — works right now, no setup

Inside any Claude Code turn, you type:

```
!pconv dump --latest --workspace-toml auto
```

Output becomes part of the conversation. One keystroke. This is already plumbed; the friction was "I didn't know about it" not "it doesn't exist."

### 2. Custom slash command — one workspace-local file

Drop this into `.claude/commands/pull-context.md` in any portagenty workspace:

```markdown
---
description: Pull the most recent session from this workspace back into context
---

Run `pconv dump --latest --workspace-toml auto --tail 80` and give me a tight
summary of what was covered. Treat it as my own prior context.
```

Now inside the session: `/pull-context` — done. The agent runs pconv, reads the output, treats it as continuation context. **Zero copy-paste.** Zero leaving the terminal.

### 3. MCP wired — natural language instead of slash commands

Once `~/.claude/mcp.json` has the portaconv entry, you just ask: *"pull in yesterday's context from this workspace."* Claude calls `list_conversations` → `get_conversation` → has it. You never type a command.

## The genuinely smooth portagenty integration (if you want it)

Here's where `pa` can help in a way that isn't just cosmetic: **`pa init` pre-wires the in-session friction killers for every workspace.** When you scaffold a workspace, `pa init` could optionally drop:

- **`.mcp.json`** with the portaconv entry — so any Claude session launched by `pa` has the MCP tools without per-session config
- **`.claude/commands/pull-context.md`** — so `/pull-context` works from moment one
- **`.claude/commands/recent-sessions.md`** — calls `pconv list --workspace-toml auto` for a quick picker

No change on portaconv's side; it's all `pa`-side scaffolding. The result: every pa-managed workspace comes with "I can reach my own history from inside Claude Code without leaving" baked in. The user never has to know portaconv exists by name.

## Does this match what you had in mind?

If yes, the picture is:

- **The TOML → portaconv mapping is path-based and already works**; `--workspace-toml auto` does exactly what you described.
- **The in-session friction problem is solvable today** via `!` prefix, `.claude/commands/`, or MCP — all accessible from inside Claude Code.
- **Portagenty can make it disappear entirely** by scaffolding those hook files into new workspaces automatically. That's the "one-evening PR on portagenty's side" I keep referencing; the file-templates aren't huge.

Want me to add a concrete **"inside Claude Code" recipe section** to the quickstart that shows all three options (`!`, custom command, MCP)? That's probably what's missing from the docs — it assumes you'll be at a shell prompt, but the realistic flow is "already inside a session and need the context NOW."

And if we need to also implement UUIDs somewhere in the mix to help with the moving paths and what not issue while keeping the claude folder naming mapping, that would be good too (although we might already be doing that)

## Assistant

## Assistant

Three threads in what you're saying — let me untangle each.

## 1. Three-way packaging + optional portagenty integration

Yes. Clean split:

| Layer | Lives where | Loads into workspace when |
|---|---|---|
| `.mcp.json` with portaconv entry | **portagenty scaffolds it** | `pa init` run with `--pconv` (or portaconv detected on PATH) |
| `.claude/commands/pull-context.md`, `recent-sessions.md`, etc. | **portagenty template, calls pconv** | Same — optional by flag, skippable if user doesn't want it |
| `.claude/skills/*.md` — a capability manifest | **could ship with either** | Same trigger |

The user never thinks about MCP vs slash commands vs `!` prefix — whichever style they prefer, it's already wired. `pa init` says "install agent hooks for portaconv? Y/n" and that's the whole UX.

## 2. The "Claude skills for discoverability" idea

You're right that this is the missing piece. Claude Code has `.claude/skills/*.md` — each file is a self-describing capability the agent discovers on session load. A pa + pconv workspace could ship with:

```
.claude/skills/
  portaconv-recover.md       # "if user asks for prior context, run pconv…"
  portaconv-commit.md        # "to persist a session to the repo, do…"
  portagenty-workspace.md    # "this is the workspace shape, available sessions…"
```

When Claude enters the session it reads these; the capabilities are *self-announcing* rather than discovered by the human via tribal knowledge. The human gets the benefit without having to learn CLI flags.

This is the real answer to "how do I tell what exists." `pa init --with-agent-hooks` (or similar) scaffolds both the plumbing AND the skills that describe it. Skills as *the map of the tools they just installed.*

## 3. UUIDs — honest answer: we're NOT doing it yet, and it matters

Current state:

- Portagenty's TOML **has** the `id` field (UUID) and portagenty uses it to survive folder moves (re-register at new path, workspace identity preserved).
- Portaconv **ignores** the `id` field today. `--workspace-toml auto` walks up to find the TOML, reads `projects = [...]`, filters by path prefix. Pure path-based.

The gap this creates: you move `~/code/myproj/` to `~/archive/myproj/`. Pa re-registers fine. But:

```
~/.claude/projects/-home-code-myproj/...        # OLD sessions, cwd=/home/code/myproj
~/.claude/projects/-home-archive-myproj/...     # NEW sessions, cwd=/home/archive/myproj
```

`pconv list --workspace-toml auto` from the new location sees `projects=["."]` → expands to `/home/archive/myproj` → finds only NEW sessions. **Old sessions are invisible.** Exactly the bridging failure the bootstrap challenge doc predicted.

### Closing it without breaking anything

Two options, I'd pick B:

**A) Id-registry coupling.** Portaconv grows `--workspace-id <uuid>`, looks up portagenty's state dir (`$XDG_STATE_HOME/portagenty/workspaces/<id>`) for current + historical paths, unions them into the scope. Pro: non-portable state (matches its nature). Con: hard coupling to pa's state layout.

**B) TOML carries the history.** Add optional `previous_paths = ["/home/code/myproj"]` to the portagenty TOML. `pa` auto-appends when it detects a re-register. `pconv` reads it along with `projects` and scopes across both. **Pro: portable, committable, no coupling to pa's state internals — just the TOML contract.** Con: TOML grows linearly with moves (fine; it's text and it's bounded).

B keeps portaconv's design intact (still path-based, just with more paths) and keeps everything in the committable TOML. The `id` field then serves as **identity for portagenty** (survives moves), and the `previous_paths` list serves as **bridging for portaconv** (knows where we've been). Complementary, not redundant.

## What I'd propose as the next build

Small, coherent batch:

1. **Portagenty PR** (upstream): `pa init --with-agent-hooks` flag that scaffolds `.mcp.json` + `.claude/commands/` + `.claude/skills/` for portaconv. Detects pconv on PATH; skips gracefully if absent.
2. **Portagenty PR** (upstream): auto-maintain `previous_paths` in the TOML when `pa` re-registers at a new location.
3. **Portaconv PR** (here): `pconv list / dump` read `previous_paths` from the TOML, expand + include in scope. One extra field parsed in the workspace-scope resolver. ~20 LOC + a test.

The skills files and command templates are the biggest content-authoring lift (a half-day to write well, not a code lift). The id/previous-paths coupling is tiny.

Want me to capture this as a "Proposed integration" section on the roadmap page so it's recorded before we drift onto the next thing? And/or add `previous_paths` to the portaconv scope resolver as a defensive no-op now — so when portagenty starts writing it, we already read it?

**tool call:** `Edit`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/mnt/c/Users/Cybersader/Documents/1 Projects, Workspaces/portaconv/src/cli.rs",
  "new_string": "fn parse_workspace_toml(path: &std::path::Path) -> Result<WorkspaceScope> {\n    // Minimal parse — we only care about two arrays:\n    //   projects       : authoritative workspace project paths\n    //   previous_paths : historical paths the workspace lived at before\n    //                    (appended by portagenty when it re-registers a\n    //                    moved folder). Bridges sessions tied to the\n    //                    old on-disk encoded-dir key in\n    //                    `~/.claude/projects/` without requiring any\n    //                    pconv-side state.\n    //\n    // A full toml dep for two array reads is overkill — line-scan it.\n    let body = std::fs::read_to_string(path)\n        .with_context(|| format!(\"read workspace toml {}\", path.display()))?;\n    let base = path\n        .parent()\n        .map(std::path::Path::to_path_buf)\n        .unwrap_or_else(|| std::path::PathBuf::from(\".\"));\n\n    let mut declared_projects: Option<Vec<std::path::PathBuf>> = None;\n    let mut previous: Vec<std::path::PathBuf> = Vec::new();\n\n    for line in body.lines() {\n        let line = line.trim();\n        if let Some(rest) = line.strip_prefix(\"previous_paths\") {\n            if let Some(items) = extract_toml_string_array(rest) {\n                for item in items {\n                    previous.push(expand_path(&item, &base));\n                }\n            }\n            continue;\n        }\n        if let Some(rest) = line.strip_prefix(\"projects\") {\n            if let Some(items) = extract_toml_string_array(rest) {\n                declared_projects = Some(\n                    items.iter().map(|s| expand_path(s, &base)).collect(),\n                );\n            }\n            continue;\n        }\n    }\n\n    // `projects` wins authoritatively when declared; otherwise fall back\n    // to the TOML's own directory (matches portagenty's convention).\n    // `previous_paths` is purely additive — always appended — so moved\n    // workspaces can reach their pre-move sessions without any\n    // portagenty-side state lookup.\n    let mut scope = WorkspaceScope::default();\n    match declared_projects {\n        Some(ps) => scope.project_paths.extend(ps),\n        None => scope.project_paths.push(base.clone()),\n    }\n    scope.project_paths.extend(previous);\n    Ok(scope)\n}\n\n/// Parse the RHS of a `key = [ \"a\", \"b\", … ]` assignment from a single\n/// TOML line. Tolerates trailing comments and inline whitespace.\n/// Returns `None` if the line isn't in the expected shape.\nfn extract_toml_string_array(rest: &str) -> Option<Vec<String>> {\n    let rhs = rest.trim_start().strip_prefix('=')?.trim();\n    // Strip an inline `# comment` tail if present; safe because TOML\n    // strings can't contain unescaped `#`-with-leading-space without\n    // being quoted, and we only match quoted items below.\n    let rhs = rhs.split_once(\" #\").map(|(a, _)| a).unwrap_or(rhs).trim();\n    let inner = rhs.strip_prefix('[').and_then(|s| s.strip_suffix(']'))?;\n    let items: Vec<String> = inner\n        .split(',')\n        .map(|s| s.trim().trim_matches(|c: char| c == '\"' || c == '\\'').to_string())\n        .filter(|s| !s.is_empty())\n        .collect();\n    Some(items)\n}",
  "old_string": "fn parse_workspace_toml(path: &std::path::Path) -> Result<WorkspaceScope> {\n    // Minimal parse — we only care about two arrays:\n    //   projects       : authoritative workspace project paths\n    //   previous_paths : historical paths the workspace lived at before\n    //                    (appended by portagenty when it re-registers a\n    //                    moved folder). Bridges sessions tied to the\n    //                    old on-disk encoded-dir key in\n    //                    `~/.claude/projects/` without requiring any\n    //                    pconv-side state.\n    //\n    // A full toml dep for two array reads is overkill — line-scan it.\n    let body = std::fs::read_to_string(path)\n        .with_context(|| format!(\"read workspace toml {}\", path.display()))?;\n    let base = path\n        .parent()\n        .map(std::path::Path::to_path_buf)\n        .unwrap_or_else(|| std::path::PathBuf::from(\".\"));\n    let mut scope = WorkspaceScope::default();\n    // Projects default to the TOML file's own directory if no\n    // `projects = [...]` line is declared — same convention portagenty\n    // uses for a workspace with no explicit project list.\n    scope.project_paths.push(base.clone());\n    let mut saw_projects = false;\n    for line in body.lines() {\n        let line = line.trim();\n        // previous_paths is purely additive — never replaces the\n        // default/declared projects. Read it here, upfront, so both\n        // orders of declarations work.\n        if let Some(rest) = line.strip_prefix(\"previous_paths\") {\n            if let Some(items) = extract_array_rhs(rest) {\n                for item in items {\n                    let expanded = expand_path(&item, &base);\n                    scope.project_paths.push(expanded);\n                }\n            }\n            continue;\n        }\n        let Some(rest) = line.strip_prefix(\"projects\") else {\n            continue;\n        };\n        let Some(rhs) = rest.trim_start().strip_prefix('=') else {\n            continue;\n        };\n        let rhs = rhs.trim();\n        let Some(inner) = rhs.strip_prefix('[').and_then(|s| s.strip_suffix(']')) else {\n            continue;\n        };\n        scope.project_paths.clear();\n        for item in inner.split(',') {\n            let item = item.trim().trim_matches(|c: char| c == '\"' || c == '\\'');\n            if item.is_empty() {\n                continue;\n            }\n            let expanded = expand_path(item, &base);\n            scope.project_paths.push(expanded);\n        }\n        break;\n    }\n    Ok(scope)\n}",
  "replace_all": false
}
```

  "new_string": "## Portagenty-side (lives in the other repo)\n\nThese ideas **aren't portaconv's to build** — they'd ship as PRs\non [portagenty](https://github.com/cybersader/portagenty). The\nreceiving-side contract (what flags pconv accepts, what output\nformat it emits) is settled and documented here; the consumer is\nupstream.\n\n- **`pa init --with-agent-hooks`** scaffolds a workspace with pconv\n  pre-wired: `.mcp.json` (portaconv MCP entry), `.claude/commands/*.md`\n  (slash commands like `/pull-context` that call pconv), and\n  `.claude/skills/*.md` (capability manifest so the agent\n  self-discovers what's available). Optional flag; skipped if\n  pconv isn't on PATH. The in-session friction killer — agent\n  inside a pa-launched session reaches its own workspace history\n  without copy-paste or leaving the terminal.\n- **`pa convos` shim.** Small wrapper that shells out to `pconv`\n  with workspace context pre-filled. `pa convos list` →\n  `pconv list --workspace-toml <current>`. `pa convos last` →\n  `pconv dump --latest --workspace-toml <current>`. **`list_includes_sessions_from_previous_paths`** in `tests/cli.rs`:

That covers: TOML parse → scope union → adapter walk → cwd filter → JSON serialization. If any link breaks, the test fails.

## Convenient dogfooding moment

This is actually the archetypal portaconv use case — you've just spent hours designing portagenty-side changes in *this* conversation, and now you want to implement them in a different workspace where a fresh Claude session has zero context. That's literally what the tool was built for.

**Concrete handoff path:**

```sh
# From anywhere (or inside this Claude Code session via ! prefix):
pconv dump --latest --workspace-toml auto --tail 200 \
  > /mnt/c/Users/Cybersader/Documents/1\ Projects,\ Workspaces/portagenty/docs/agent-context/2026-04-21-portaconv-integration-plan.md

cd "../portagenty"
git add docs/agent-context/
git commit -m "context: portaconv integration design from 2026-04-21"
```

Then switch to the portagenty workspace and either:
- **Start a fresh Claude session there**, which auto-reads repo files (you'd mention the context doc in your first prompt), or
- **Paste the markdown directly into a new session's first message**

You'll walk in with the whole design discussion preloaded — no re-explaining MCP wiring, no re-debating `previous_paths` vs id-registry, no re-derivation of why the TOML is the portable contract.

Want me to:
1. **Generate that handoff doc now** — trim this session down to the portagenty-implementation-relevant parts (skip the path-poisoning spike, skip the Rust code discussions, keep the integration design) and write it to the portagenty repo?
2. **Or leave it to you** — you pick which flavor (full dump / custom trim / direct paste) and handle the switch yourself?

Either works. If you want option 1, say the word and I'll run the commands.

The right move is to let you start a fresh Claude session in the portagenty workspace with this handoff doc as context — that way the new agent gets to explore portagenty's codebase properly and its own conversation history lives in portagenty's bucket, not portaconv's.
